Composição florística e estrutura da regeneração natural do Parque Estadual do Espinilho, RS.

Cristina Gouvêa Redin, Régis Villanova Longhi, Luciano Farinha Watzlawick, Solon Jonas Longhi (2011)

Abstract

O presente estudo teve como objetivo avaliar a composição florística, diversidade, padrões de distribuição espacial e estrutura da regeneração natural das espécies arbóreas em Savana Estépica Parque, localizada no Parque Estadual do Espinilho, extremo sudoeste do Estado do Rio Grande do Sul, Brasil. Essa tipologia abriga uma vegetação peculiar, não ocorrendo em outras áreas do país, com presença de espécies endêmicas e vulneráveis. Para a análise, foi instalada uma unidade amostral permanente de 4ha (200x200m) subdividida em 400 subunidades de 100m² (10x10m) cada. Dessas, foram sorteadas 60 subunidades, em que todos os indivíduos com altura superior a 30cm e diâmetro ao nível do solo (DNS) tomado a ±03cm de altura, inferior a 9,5cm foram amostrados. Foram encontrados 174 indivíduos, distribuídos em cinco famílias botânicas, seis gêneros e seis espécies. A regeneração natural apresentou Índice de Diversidade de Shannon estimado em 0,82, indicando resultados baixos para a diversidade de espécies. As espécies com maiores valores de importância foram Vachellia caven (Molina) Molina (63,96%) e Celtis ehrenbergiana (Klotzsch) Liebm. (30%). Essas duas espécies apresentaram comportamento agregado, enquanto Prosopis affinis Spreng., espécie característica do parque, obteve comportamento não agregado segundo o Índice de Payandeh. A regeneração natural da área não se encontra balanceada, entretanto segue o modelo “J invertido”, apresentando déficit de indivíduos na classe inicial de diâmetro, possivelmente devido ao pastoreio atualmente realizado no local.

Main Points

The study analyzed the natural regeneration of arboreal species in 60 randomly selected subunits (10x10m) within a 4ha plot in the Steppe Savannah Park (Savana Estépica Parque), Parque Estadual do Espinilho, RS. The regeneration phase included individuals taller than 30 cm and with a diameter at soil level (DNS) lower than 9.5 cm.

A total of 174 individuals, distributed among five families, six genera, and six species, were sampled, resulting in an estimated density of 292 individuals per hectare. The floristic diversity was low (Shannon Index H’ = 0.82), and the vegetation uniformity was poor (Pielou Equitability J = 0.46), primarily due to extreme species dominance. The species with the highest Importance Values (VI) were **Vachellia caven** (64.03%) and *Celtis ehrenbergiana* (29.94%), together accounting for approximately 94% of the VI.

Only *Vachellia caven* (193 ind.ha⁻¹) and *Prosopis affinis* (5 ind.ha⁻¹) were found regenerating among the species typical of the Park. Both *Vachellia caven* and *Celtis ehrenbergiana* exhibited an **aggregated spatial distribution** (PI > 1.5). Conversely, *Prosopis affinis*, despite being a characteristic park species, showed an aleatory (non-aggregated) distribution (PI = 0.97). Analysis of the diameter distribution revealed that the regeneration structure, although following the inverse J-shape model, showed a significant deficit of individuals in the initial diameter class.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the natural regeneration in the Steppe Savannah Park exhibits low diversity and uniformity, dominated strongly by *Vachellia caven* and *Celtis ehrenbergiana*. The composition and structure suggest that the ecosystem's characteristic arboreal species, particularly *Prosopis affinis* and *Prosopis nigra*, are struggling with self-regeneration and recruitment.

This negative outcome is strongly attributed to **anthropogenic impacts**. The population structure's observed deficit in the initial diameter classes is linked to current grazing activity (*pastoreio*) in the area. The study also cites external literature noting that environmental impacts such as cattle creation and fire management, particularly in areas of *Prosopis* distribution, cause severe damage and lead to **invasion by thorny shrubs** of the genera *Vachellia*, *Celtis*, and *Mimosa*.

This invasion results in dense scrubland, ultimately hindering the natural regeneration of the typical arboreal species of the Savana Estépica Parque. The conclusion emphasizes that human activities like habitat conversion and intensive grazing are reducing the coverage area of this unique, endemic, and vulnerable vegetation type, underscoring the necessity of conservation studies in the region.

  • "As espécies com maiores valores de importância foram Vachellia caven (Molina) Molina (63,96%) e Celtis ehrenbergiana (Klotzsch) Liebm. (30%)."

  • "Essa tipologia abriga uma vegetação peculiar, não ocorrendo em outras áreas do país, com presença de espécies endêmicas e vulneráveis."
  • "A utilização com atividade de pecuária interfere muito na regeneração natural das espécies arbóreas do local."
  • "No Bosque Chaquenho Argentino, segundo TÁLAMO et al. (2009), a criação de gado causa modificação da regeneração natural das espécies, compactação do solo por pisoteio, dispersão de sementes de espécies forrageiras, além de estimular o rebrote de raízes de certas espécies e determinar um efeito seletivo na vegetação."
  • "Nos últimos anos, segundo WATZLAWICK et al. (2010), esta vegetação vem sofrendo intensa antropização, principalmente devido à mudança do uso da terra, na qual a vegetação nativa é substituída por pastagens, para o cultivo de grãos, ou mesmo utilizada para o pastoreio de forma intensiva."

(2003), o impacto ambiental causado em áreas de distribuição natural do gênero Prosopis para criação de gado e o emprego do fogo para manejo de pastagens está causando grandes danos a essa vegetação, como a invasão por espécies arbustivas espinhosas do gênero Vachellia, Celtis e Mimosa."
Supports Soil and Biogeochemical CyclingPampas Ecosystem Degradation and ResilienceGrazing and Land Use Impacts

Nitrogen mineralization potential depletion in pampas (Argentina) croplands following conversion from native grasslands

Nicolas Wyngaard, Cecilia Crespo, Gisela Vanesa García, Nahuel Ignacio Reussi Calvo, Camila Rivero, Walter Daniel Carciochi, Mercedes Eyherabide, Gastón Larrea, Hernán Angelini, Pablo Barbieri, Hernán Rene Sainz Rozas (2025)

Abstract

In the Argentinean Pampas, where Phaeozems soils are predominant, the conversion of native grasslands into croplands has negatively affected soil fertility and health. Nitrogen (N) mineralized during an anaerobic incubation (Nan), an estimator of N potential mineralization, is frequently used to evaluate soil health. The objectives of our study were to determine the magnitude of the Nan depletion caused by agriculture (dNan), and to assess the relative contribution of land use, climate, and soil properties on dNan in the Argentinean Pampas. We conducted a soil survey at 409 sites distributed throughout the Argentinean Pampas region. At each site, pairwise samples (0–20 cm) were collected from uncultivated and agricultural soils. At each site, different edaphic, climatic, and productive variables were evaluated. The direct and indirect effect of different variables over dNan was evaluated through a path analysis. The conversion of native grasslands from the Argentinean Pampas into croplands generally decreased Nan values, with Nan reductions ranging from 0 to 216 mg kg−1 (representing 0 to 79 % of the Nan value at uncultivated soils). The magnitude of the Nan depletion was influenced by edaphic variables [i.e. original Nan value (Nan at uncropped soils), soil organic matter depletion, clay content] and climatic variables (i.e. precipitation). These four variables explained 85 % of the dNan variability. From the path analysis, it was determined that soils with greater original Nan values (r = 0.89) and greater soil organic matter depletion (r = 0.65) presented larger dNan, while increases in clay content (r = 0.30) or mean annual precipitation (r = 0.25) resulted in lower dNan values. The identification of the drivers of Nan depletion can aid in the classification of areas with greater vulnerability to soil degradation and in the development of models to predict Nan depletion in soils. Such models would hold significant potential as tools for policymakers and program developers engaged in the formulation and implementation of targeted interventions aimed at halting or reversing this degradation process.

Main Points

The study utilized a large-scale soil survey across 409 paired sites throughout the Argentinean Pampas (Phaeozems soils) to determine the magnitude and drivers of Nitrogen mineralization potential depletion (dNan) following the conversion of native grasslands (UC) to croplands (AGR).

Methodologically, researchers collected pairwise samples (0–20 cm) and analyzed edaphic (Nan, SOM, pH, texture), climatic (precipitation, temperature), and land-use variables (soybean cultivation intensity) at each location. The difference in Nan between uncropped and agricultural sites (dNan) was used as the indicator of soil health degradation. A path analysis was then performed to assess the direct and indirect causal effects of the collected variables on dNan.

Results demonstrated that agriculturization consistently decreased Nan values, with reductions ranging from 0 to 79% of the original Nan value in native soils, equating to losses up to 216 mg kg⁻¹. The path analysis identified four key variables explaining 85% of the dNan variability: original Nan value (Nan-UC, r=0.89), Soil Organic Matter depletion (dSOM, r=0.65), clay content (r=0.30), and mean annual precipitation (PPm, r=0.25). Sites starting with higher Nan values and those suffering greater SOM depletion showed the largest dNan (greatest degradation), while higher clay content and precipitation provided a mitigating effect, resulting in lower dNan values.

Conclusions

The study definitively concludes that the conversion of native grasslands into croplands in the Argentinean Pampas has resulted in a significant and widespread loss of Nitrogen mineralization potential (Nan), confirming substantial degradation of soil fertility and health.

The variability in Nan depletion (dNan) across the region is primarily controlled by a combination of edaphic and climatic factors. The most critical drivers of degradation magnitude are the soil’s initial N fertility (Nan-UC) and the degree of SOM depletion caused by agriculture. Conversely, physical properties like clay content and climatic factors like precipitation offer crucial buffering capacity, reducing the magnitude of Nan loss.

These findings are framed as essential tools for conservation efforts. The identification of degradation drivers allows researchers to classify regions highly vulnerable to future soil loss and develop predictive models for Nan depletion. The authors emphasize that these models are vital resources for policymakers, enabling the creation of targeted interventions and sustainable management programs aimed at halting or reversing the negative consequences of intense agriculturization in the Pampas region.

Key Quotes

  • "Nitrogen (N) mineralized during an anaerobic incubation (Nan), an estimator of N potential mineralization, is frequently used to evaluate soil health."
  • "The conversion of native grasslands from the Argentinean Pampas into croplands generally decreased Nan values, with Nan reductions ranging from 0 to 216 mg kg−1 (representing 0 to 79 % of the Nan value at uncultivated soils)."
  • "Soil organic matter (SOM) content in the soil significantly decreased as a result of this change in land use... and, because SOM contains most soil nitrogen (N), its depletion significantly impacts soil N fertility."
  • "Therefore, the estimation of the N mineralization potential of soils is critical to determining N availability for crops (Orcellet et al., 2016; Reussi Calvo et al., 2018)."
  • "Moreover, the Nan has been recently proposed as a soil health indicator, due to its sensitivity to management practices and land use changes..."
  • "However, there are no large-scale studies identifying the main drivers (i.e. climate, soil, and land use variables) of Nan changes caused by agriculture."
  • "One of the edaphic properties that influence Nan values is the SOM content (Schomberg et al., 2009; Wyngaard et al., 2018)."
  • "From the path analysis, it was determined that soils with greater original Nan values (r = 0.89) and greater soil organic matter depletion (r = 0.65) presented larger dNan..."
  • "Such models would hold significant potential as tools for policymakers and program developers engaged in the formulation and implementation of targeted interventions aimed at halting or reversing this degradation process."

Megafauna biogeography explains plant functional trait variability in the tropics

Vinicius L. Dantas | Juli G. Pausas (2020)

Abstract

Aim: Biomes can diverge substantially in plant functional traits and disturbance regimens among regions. Given that Neotropical and Afrotropical regions have contrasting histories of the megafauna (because of the Holocene megafaunal extinction in the Neotropics), we hypothesize that they should harbour plants with different traits in relationship to herbivory and fire, especially in savannas. We predicted that herbivory resistance traits should be more prominent in Afrotropical savanna plants and fire resistance in Neotropical savanna plants. Location: Tropics. Time period: Not applicable. Major taxa studied: Angiosperms (woody). Methods: We compiled data for five key plant functional traits (wood density, specific leaf area, maximum tree height, spinescence and proportion of geoxyles) for forest and savanna woody species from the two distant regions (Afrotropics and Neotropics). We related these data to climate, soil and fire variables and tested predictions for megafauna selection. Results: Spines and high wood density were more common among Afrotropical than Neotropical savanna species and species from the two forests. Moreover, the Neotropical savanna region contained more geoxyles than the Afrotropical savanna region. Finally, Afrotropical species were taller than Neotropical species. These differences were consistent with our predictions for trait selection by the megafauna, and these patterns did not change when considering climate, soil and fire regimens in the models. Main conclusions: Our results highlight the great potential of these traits for summarizing disturbance strategy axes in tropical woody species and suggest that global variation in plant traits is unlikely to be understood fully without consideration of historical factors, especially the direct and indirect impacts of megafauna.

Main Points

The researchers aimed to determine if the contrasting histories of megafauna in the Neotropics (post-Holocene extinction) and Afrotropics (retaining megafauna) resulted in differing plant functional traits related to herbivory and fire resistance in savannas. The study compiled data for five key traits: wood density (WD), specific leaf area (SLA), maximum tree height (HMax), spinescence (presence/absence), and the proportion of geoxyles across woody species in forest and savanna biomes in both regions. These comparisons utilized linear mixed-effect models, also factoring in climate, soil, and fire variables to isolate the impact of historical megafauna selection.

The results largely confirmed the megafauna selection hypothesis. Spines and high wood density, traits associated with mechanical resistance against large browsers, were significantly more prevalent among Afrotropical savanna species compared to Neotropical savanna species. Conversely, the Neotropical savanna region exhibited a higher proportion of geoxyles (underground trees)—a trait essential for fire survival—than the Afrotropical region. Furthermore, Afrotropical species were generally taller than Neotropical species. Crucially, these biogeographical differences, aligning with predictions of differential megafauna pressure, were found to be statistically robust and persisted even when environmental variables like climate, soil, and contemporary fire regimes were included in the statistical models.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the analyzed functional traits serve as excellent indicators for summarizing disturbance strategy axes among tropical woody species. The primary finding is that global variation in plant functional traits cannot be adequately understood without incorporating historical factors, particularly the direct and indirect impacts stemming from megafauna.

Specifically, the trait divergence observed between the Afrotropical and Neotropical savannas reflects different historical selection pressures. The sustained presence of megaherbivores in Africa selected for strong herbivory defense traits (spines, high WD), while the loss of megafauna in the Neotropics likely led to a decrease in grazing pressure, favoring the shift toward fire-maintained ecosystems and the dominance of fire-resistance strategies, such as geoxyly. This emphasizes that while current ecological drivers are important, deep historical processes fundamentally modulate the adaptive strategies and biogeographical divergence of plant communities.

Key Quotes

  • "Given that Neotropical and Afrotropical regions have contrasting histories of the megafauna (because of the Holocene megafaunal extinction in the Neotropics), we hypothesize that they should harbour plants with different traits in relationship to herbivory and fire, especially in savannas."
  • "We predicted that herbivory resistance traits should be more prominent in Afrotropical savanna plants and fire resistance in Neotropical savanna plants."
  • "Results: Spines and high wood density were more common among Afrotropical than Neotropical savanna species and species from the two forests."
  • "These differences were consistent with our predictions for trait selection by the megafauna, and these patterns did not change when considering climate, soil and fire regimens in the models."
  • "Our results highlight the great potential of these traits for summarizing disturbance strategy axes in tropical woody species and suggest that global variation in plant traits is unlikely to be understood fully without consideration of historical factors, especially the direct and indirect impacts of megafauna."
  • "A high WD would provide mechanical stability not only to forest trees... but also to savanna plants exposed to breakage by large browsers (e.g., elephants)."
  • "Many studies are also showing that plants with spines and densely branched crowns are favoured and even evolved in response to megaherbivores in African savannas."
  • "In contrast, plants with specialized woody bud-bearing underground structures (geoxyles or 'underground trees') are also favoured and evolved in fire-maintained ecosystems where herbivory is low (e.g., wet regions...)."
  • "The present and historical lack of megagrazers to control grass biomass and promote herbivory-maintained savannas in the Neotropics might have favoured more savannas maintained by high-intensity surface fires..."
  • "To test our hypothesis, we compiled data on spinescence (presence/absence), HMax (in metres), SLA (in square millimetres per milligram), and WD (in grams per cubic centimetre) for Afrotropical and Neotropical savanna and forest species."

Recuperación del pastizal natural en un bosque nativo degradado del Espinal argentino mediante el control químico aéreo de arbustivas

Julián Alberto Sabattini, Rafael Alberto Sabattini, Florencia Urteaga Omar, Mauricio Bacigalupo, Juan Carlos Cian, Iván Alberto Sabattini y Víctor Manuel Dopazo (2019)

Abstract

La estabilidad de los ecosistemas está directamente relacionada con un alto valor de biodiversidad y, en este sentido, los efectos antrópicos han generado condiciones negativas sobre los pastizales naturales. El objetivo del trabajo fue evaluar la respuesta del pastizal natural de un bosque nativo degradado del Espinal argentino con arbustivas por medio de un control químico aéreo en un sistema ganadero con pastoreo rotativo de baja carga instantánea. El estudio se realizó en el Área Natural Protegida Reserva de Usos Múltiples Estancia "El Carayá" ubicada en el centro-norte de Entre Ríos, Argentina. Se realizaron 16 evaluaciones desde el año 2012 al 2015 sobre el sector tratado químicamente con Picloram+2,4-D y tres sectores sin tratamiento. En cada evaluación se cuantificó la cobertura vegetal, la composición florística de las especies forrajeras más representativas y la biomasa vegetal, comparadas mediante pruebas no paramétricas. Los resultados de este trabajo comprueban que la utilización de una técnica de control químico aéreo aumentó significativamente, un 44%, la cobertura y biomasa en las áreas tratadas de las especies forrajeras respecto al testigo. El control químico sobre las arbustivas persistió en el tiempo con una efectividad considerable durante los años de evaluación. Por otro lado, la composición florística de las especies herbáceas no presentó diferencias significativas entre tratamientos.

Main Points

The study was conducted in the Protected Natural Area Reserve of Multiple Uses Estancia "El Carayá" in north-central Entre Ríos, Argentina, within the Espinal Phytogeographic Province. The area is characterized by degraded native forest suffering from *arbustización* (shrub encroachment), primarily caused by bovine overgrazing. The dominant invading species include *Baccharis punctulata*, *Eupatorium buniifolium*, and *Aloysia gratissima*.

The research aimed to evaluate the effectiveness of aerial chemical control in recovering natural grassland for cattle grazing. On April 20, 2012, an 85 ha sector was treated with an aerial application of Picloram + 2,4-D (4 L ha-1 commercial product), known to be a systemic herbicide targeting broadleaf weeds while sparing gramineous species and mature trees. A low instantaneous load rotary grazing system was maintained throughout the study period.

Sixteen evaluations were performed between 2012 and 2015 on the treated sector and three untreated control sectors. Researchers quantified vegetation cover (categorized into forage species, specific target shrubs, and other non-forage species), floristic composition using the Braun-Blanquet method, and plant biomass. The results demonstrated that the use of aerial chemical control significantly increased the coverage and biomass of desirable forage species by 44% compared to the control areas. Furthermore, the chemical control over the shrubs persisted effectively during the years of evaluation. However, the floristic composition of the herbaceous species (beyond simple coverage/biomass gain) did not show significant differences between treated and untreated sectors.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that anthropogenic effects, such as overgrazing, have created negative conditions on natural pastures, leading to shrub encroachment (*arbustización*). This encroachment reduces the accessibility and availability of forage for cattle, justifying management intervention.

The findings validate the use of aerial chemical control (Picloram+2,4-D) as a successful technique to reverse shrub encroachment in degraded native forests of the Argentine Espinal. The increased coverage and biomass of forage species (a 44% increase) confirm the economic benefit for livestock production and the successful ecological manipulation toward a grassland state.

Critically, the paper frames the woody species as weeds (*malezas*) that compete for essential resources (light, water, nutrients) with the desirable herbaceous layer. The sustained effectiveness of the chemical control over the evaluation period supports the continued application of this management strategy for reversing grassland degradation caused by the proliferation of *arbustivas*.

FLORÍSTICA E CARBONO DO SOLO E DA SERAPILHEIRA EM CAMPOS E FLORESTAS DO BIOMA PAMPA COM DIFERENTES NÍVEIS DE CONSERVAÇÃO

Jocimar Caiafa Milagre (2023)

Abstract

Uma ampla variedade de serviços ecossistêmicos relacionados à biodiversidade e ao armazenamento de carbono (C) é fornecida por campos e florestas do bioma Pampa. Apesar da importância desses serviços, é rápida a conversão de áreas naturais nessa região do Brasil. O objetivo deste estudo foi avaliar a florística e o estoque de C do solo e da serapilheira em áreas de campo e mata ciliar com distintos níveis de conservação no Pampa. As áreas de estudo foram denominadas como voçoroca (V), campo degradado (CD), campo conservado (CC), mata degradada (MD) e mata conservada (MC). V é uma área em processo avançado de erosão, composta por duas voçorocas. CD é uma área de campo nativo com carga animal de 310 kg de peso vivo por hectare e invasão biológica por Eragrostis plana Nees. CC também é uma área de campo nativo, porém manejada com carga animal de 170 kg de peso vivo por hectare. MD e MC são áreas de mata ciliar contíguas, sendo MD manejada com gado e MC isolada do gado. No levantamento florístico foram avaliadas a abundância e riqueza de espécies em parcelas de 1 m x 1 m (V, CD e CC), 10 m x 20 m (estrato arbóreo de MD e MC) e 10 m x 10 m (regeneração natural de MD e MC). Em cada área de estudo foram coletadas 20 amostras de serapilheira e cinco amostras de solo compostas nas profundidades de 0-5, 5-15, 15-30 e 30-100 cm. Foram determinados os teores de C e nitrogênio (N) e razão isotópica natural e calculados os Índices de Diversidade de Shannon (H’) e Equabilidade de Pielou (J’). Os dados de solo e serapilheira foram submetidos à ANOVA e teste de Tukey (p<0,05). Os dados de abundância, riqueza, diversidade e equabilidade das áreas de campo (V, CD e CC) foram submetidos ao teste de Kruskall-Wallis (p<0,05), seguido pelo teste de Dunn. Para comparar as médias de abundância, riqueza, diversidade e equabilidade do estrato arbóreo e regeneração natural das áreas de mata ciliar (MD e MC) foi realizada a ANOVA (teste F, p<0,05). No levantamento florístico foram amostrados 5.798 indivíduos, distribuídos em 38 famílias e 134 espécies. A abundância de indivíduos de V e CC foi diferente, mas não houve diferenças entre V, CD e CC para riqueza, H’ e J’. Nas matas ciliares, o uso pelo gado reduziu a abundância no estrato arbóreo e diminuiu drasticamente a abundância, riqueza e H’ na regeneração natural. A serapilheira se mostrou como um importante compartimento que armazena C nas áreas de campo e mata ciliar e seu acúmulo foi impactado pela degradação. A degradação modificou a composição de espécies e o estoque de C da serapilheira nas áreas de campo. O maior grau de degradação do solo em V diminuiu o estoque de C em relação a CD. O uso pelo gado impactou a estrutura e composição florística das áreas de mata ciliar, mas não alterou o estoque de C do solo. Os resultados deste estudo reforçam a importância do bioma Pampa na manutenção da biodiversidade vegetal e armazenamento de C no solo e serapilheira e podem apoiar a implementação de políticas públicas de conservação e restauração.

Main Points

The study's objective was to analyze floristics and Carbon (C) stocks in soil and litter across five land use conditions in the Pampa biome near Alegrete, RS: Gully (V, advanced erosion), Degraded Grassland (CD, high grazing intensity at 310 kg/ha, plus *Eragrostis plana* invasion), Conserved Grassland (CC, low grazing intensity at 170 kg/ha), Degraded Riparian Forest (MD, managed with cattle), and Conserved Riparian Forest (MC, isolated from cattle).

A comprehensive floristic survey was conducted, sampling 5,798 individuals belonging to 38 families and 134 species. Soil samples were collected at four depth intervals (0–5, 5–15, 15–30, 30–100 cm) and 20 litter samples were taken per area. C and Nitrogen (N) content, natural isotopic ratio, and diversity indices (Shannon H', Pielou J') were measured.

The results demonstrated significant ecological impacts tied to degradation, especially grazing. In grasslands, while severe erosion (V) reduced C stock relative to CD, abundance, richness, and diversity indices (H' and J') did not show significant differences between V, CD, and CC, though degradation did modify species composition and litter C stock. Litter was confirmed as an important C compartment whose accumulation was sensitive to degradation.

In riparian forests, the presence of cattle (MD) significantly reduced overall abundance in the tree stratum. Critically, grazing drastically diminished the abundance, richness, and Shannon Diversity Index (H') of the natural regeneration layer compared to the conserved area (MC), indicating severe inhibition of forest recovery. Although cattle use impacted the structure and floristic composition of the riparian forests, it did not significantly alter the total C stock of the soil.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the Pampa biome holds significant importance for both the maintenance of plant biodiversity and the storage of carbon in both the soil and the litter layer. The observed rapid conversion of natural areas highlights the vulnerability of the Pampa's ecosystem services.

Overall degradation, exemplified by intense grazing pressure and erosion, was shown to be the primary driver negatively affecting ecosystem function. Specifically, high animal stocking rates severely suppressed the natural regeneration of riparian forests, posing a long-term threat to the maintenance and recovery of these woody ecosystems. Degradation also altered the specific composition of grassland species and reduced carbon stocks in the litter layer and severely eroded soils.

The findings reinforce the necessity of implementing improved land management strategies. The study explicitly states that its results are valuable scientific evidence that can support the development and implementation of effective public policies aimed at conservation and ecological restoration within the Pampa biome.

  • "Apesar da importância desses serviços, é rápida a conversão de áreas naturais nessa região do Brasil."
  • "CD é uma área de campo nativo com carga animal de 310 kg de peso vivo por hectare e invasão biológica por Eragrostis plana Nees."
  • "Nas matas ciliares, o uso pelo gado reduziu a abundância no estrato arbóreo e diminuiu drasticamente a abundância, riqueza e H’ na regeneração natural."
  • "A serapilheira se mostrou como um importante compartimento que armazena C nas áreas de campo e mata ciliar e seu acúmulo foi impactado pela degradação."
  • "A degradação modificou a composição de espécies e o estoque de C da serapilheira nas áreas de campo."
  • "O maior grau de degradação do solo em V diminuiu o estoque de C em relação a CD."
  • "O uso pelo gado impactou a estrutura e composição florística das áreas de mata ciliar, mas não alterou o estoque de C do solo."
  • "Os resultados deste estudo reforçam a importância do bioma Pampa na manutenção da biodiversidade vegetal e armazenamento de C no solo e serapilheira..."

The Brazilian Pampa: A Fragile Biome

Luiz Fernando Wurdig Roesch, Frederico Costa Beber Vieira, Vilmar Alves Pereira, Adriano Luis Schünemann, Italo Filippi Teixeira, Ana Julia Teixeira Senna and Valdir Marcos Stefenon (2009)

Abstract

Biodiversity is one of the most fundamental properties of Nature. It underpins the stability of ecosystems, provides vast bioresources for economic use, and has important cultural significance for many people. The Pampa biome, located in the southernmost state of Brazil, Rio Grande do Sul, illustrates the direct and indirect interdependence of humans and biodiversity. The Brazilian Pampa lies within the South Temperate Zone where grasslands scattered with shrubs and trees are the dominant vegetation. The soil, originating from sedimentary rocks, often has an extremely sandy texture that makes them fragile—highly prone to water and wind erosion. Human activities have converted or degraded many areas of this biome. In this review we discuss our state-of-the-art knowledge of the diversity and the major biological features of this regions and the cultural factors that have shaped it. Our aim is to contribute toward a better understanding of the current status of this special biome and to describe how the interaction between human activities and the environment affects the region, highlighting the fragility of the Brazilian Pampa.

Main Points

This review analyzes the diversity and intense degradation challenges facing the Brazilian Pampa, the second smallest Brazilian biome, located primarily in Rio Grande do Sul. The authors emphasize that the biome's fragility stems from its geology and soil properties. The region comprises four geological provinces, and soils derived from sedimentary rocks often possess an extremely sandy texture (especially Psamment soils/Neossolos Quartzarenicos in the Central Depression and parts of the Serra Geral Formation).

This inherent soil fragility, which makes them highly sensitive to water and wind erosion, is severely exacerbated by inappropriate human activities. Livestock production is historically a main economic activity based on natural grasslands, but alongside agriculture, overgrazing has contributed to intense soil degradation. A specific and devastating process, termed 'sandification,' occurs where sandy soils lose clay, silt, and organic matter, leading to nutrient depletion and loss of soil cohesion. These degraded areas, characterized by extensive sand patches, are difficult to reverse and expand through intense eolic erosion, creating a positive feedback cycle.

Regarding conservation, the authors discuss restoration strategies for sandification sites. Revegetation is considered the most successful recovery method, but plant establishment is difficult. While fast-growing exotic species (e.g., *Eucalyptus sp*, *Pinus sp*) have been proposed for their resistance, the review notes this approach is controversial, with counterarguments favoring the use of native plants.

Conclusions

The review concludes that the critical issue facing the Brazilian Pampa is its inherent fragility, primarily defined by geological composition that yields easily erodible, often sandy, soils. This natural susceptibility is greatly magnified by intensive and inappropriate human land-use practices, such as agriculture and overgrazing.

The resulting intense soil degradation, including severe erosion and sandification, is not only an ecological crisis but also contributes significantly to socio-economic fragility, as evidenced by low Social Development Indices in the affected region. The authors stress that effective conservation requires deep knowledge of the soil characteristics, potential, and limitations, especially since vast areas dominated by fragile soil types (Udults, Psamments, Orthents) place strong limitations on intensive agrosilvopastoral systems.

Ultimately, the paper aims to contribute to a better understanding of this unique biome's current status and to highlight the urgent need for appropriate conservation management practices to ensure environmental and socioeconomic sustainability, contrasting the Pampa's decline with the status of other major Brazilian biomes.

Key Quotes

  • "The soil, originating from sedimentary rocks, often has an extremely sandy texture that makes them fragile—highly prone to water and wind erosion."
  • "Human activities have converted or degraded many areas of this biome."
  • "Because of the natural grasslands, livestock production is one of the main economic activities; they are a source of forage for around 18 million animals—mainly cattle and sheep [4]."
  • "The geologic material makes the soils fragile—they are highly sensitive to water and wind erosion."
  • "The natural fragility of the soil, combined with the climatic conditions means that inappropriate human activities have led to intense soil degradation."
  • "The natural fragility of the soil, combined with the climatic conditions means that inappropriate human activities have led to intense soil degradation. This in turn has contributed to a socio-economic fragility as evidenced by the low Social Development Index of the region [5]."
  • "Psamment soils (Neossolos Quartzarenicos) are found here, in areas that were not covered by the magmatic extrusion or where the cover of basalt has weathered [14]. The fragility of these soils facilitates their degradation."
  • "After the natural vegetation is lost soil organic matter becomes depleted, and the chemical, physical and biological properties of the soil become severely degraded..."
  • "The degradation has been exacerbated by agricultural and overgrazing activities (Figure 2b,c)."

Uso e manejo de herbicidas em pastagens

Maurílio Fernandes de Oliveira, Ivan Jannotti Wendling, Márcia Cristina Teixeira da Silveira (2019)

Abstract

A pecuária brasileira vem buscando modernizar os sistemas de produção, com o objetivo de aumentar a produtividade com sustentabilidade. A adoção de práticas agrícolas no manejo da pastagem possibilita maior produtividade, evitando degradação, que está geralmente associada a menor quantidade ou mesmo à ausência da forrageira e à presença de grande quantidade de plantas daninhas. Em áreas com degração avançada, o programa de manejo das plantas daninhas deve ser utilizado em conjunto com práticas agrícolas de recuperação ou reforma da pastagem. O controle químico das plantas daninhas em pastagem vem sendo utilizado largamente nos sistemas de produção animal convencional. Alta eficiência no uso dos herbicidas ocorre quando há identificação da planta daninha e escolha do herbicida adequado. O uso e manejo de herbicidas em pastagem deve priorizar entendimento amplo da implantação e do manejo da pastagem, correlacionando-o com o possível aparecimento das plantas daninhas. Vale ressaltar que o método mais eficaz e barato é a prevenção. Logo, o bom manejo de estabelecimento e uso das pastagens pode ser um grande aliado no controle de plantas daninhas e a ele ser associado o controle químico adequado. Assim, o sucesso no programa de manejo das plantas daninhas com herbicidas demandará adequada seleção dentre as formulações disponíveis no mercado, seu manuseio correto e avaliação na eficiência do programa de manejo adotado. Este documento tem o objetivo de demonstrar que um programa de manejo de invasoras é prática importante, porém não se apresenta como solução única para garantir aumento na produtividade da pastagem.

Main Points

The document, published by Embrapa, details the causes and methods for controlling weeds in grazing areas, driven by the goal of increasing productivity and capacity support (UA/ha). Weed infestation, particularly by broadleaf plants, is attributed to inadequate implementation practices (poor soil preparation, insufficient fertilization) and improper usage (sub- or super-grazing, burning).

The document outlines five main control methods: cultural (using aggressive forage cultivars), physical (fire), manual, mechanical (mowing), and chemical (herbicides). It strongly advocates for an integrated approach where chemical control is associated with global management improvements (correction, fertilization, load adjustment).

Key steps for effective chemical control include: 1) Verifying the remaining density of desirable forage species (if the area is too degraded, recovery or renovation is recommended); 2) Identifying the weed species to determine susceptibility; 3) Considering the foliage type, as tough leaves require specific additives or application methods (like stump application); and 4) Applying systemic herbicides during full vegetative development (rainy season), as efficacy drops significantly during flowering/fruiting when translocation to roots is reduced.

The text identifies woody species (shrubs and subshrubs) as the 'principal problem' in pastures, listing examples such as *Mata-pasto*, *Assa-peixe*, and various thorny species (*Unha-de-gato*). It emphasizes that good grazing management, specifically managing pasture height based on light interception (90% to 95%), acts as a preventive strategy by ensuring forage plant persistence and competitiveness, thereby minimizing the need for reactive weed control.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that while a weed management program, often relying on chemical control, is important, it is not a singular solution for guaranteeing increased pasture productivity. The most effective, cheapest, and primary method is prevention, achieved through the successful establishment and appropriate, continuous management of the pasture.

Good management—including soil correction, adequate fertilization, and proper adjustment of livestock load—is identified as the greatest ally against weeds. When chemical control is necessary, success requires proper selection of available formulations, correct handling, and continuous evaluation of the program's efficiency.

The overarching goal is to modernize Brazilian livestock systems to achieve greater productivity with sustainability, aligning the recommendations for responsible herbicide use with global objectives like SDG 12 (Sustainable Consumption and Production). The document reinforces the perspective that any species inhibiting forage production must be controlled or eliminated.

  • "...a eliminação destas plantas daninhas é problema com que todo pecuarista depara-se constantemente..."
  • "O controle químico é um método rápido e necessita de menos mão de obra."
  • "A utilização de herbicidas, ao acabar com a competição causada pelas plantas daninhas, ajuda no aumento da produção de massa verde na pastagem, e consequentemente no aumento da capacidade de suporte."

  • "Deve-se escolher o herbicida e o aditivo (espalhante adesivo) apropriados para facilitar a absorção."

Espécies de Plantas Prioritárias para Projetos de Restauração Ecológica em Diferentes Formações Vegetais no Bioma Pampa: Primeira Aproximação

Ernestino de Souza Gomes Guarino, Gerhard Ernst Overbeck, Ilsi Iob Boldrini, Sandra Cristina Mulller, Ana Paula Rovedder, Thales Castilhos de Freitas, Gustavo Crizel Gomes, André Hildebrandt Noronha, Adalberto Koiti Miura, Letícia Penno de Sousa, Danilo Menezes Sant’Anna, Luiza Chomenko, Martin Molz, Jan Karel Felix Mahler Júnior, Artur Ramos Molina, Vinicius Schmalfuss Espindola (2018)

Abstract

Not found. This document, published in the 'Documentos' series by Embrapa, does not include a formal Abstract (Resumo) section in the introductory pages provided.

Main Points

This document addresses the urgent necessity for ecological restoration in the Pampa Biome, which is restricted to Rio Grande do Sul and has experienced accelerated agricultural expansion, particularly the conversion of native grasslands into monocultures (soy, rice) and exotic tree plantations (eucalyptus, pine). Current data indicates that 48.7% of the Pampa Biome is currently under anthropogenic use.

The drive for this restoration work stems from recent legislative mandates, specifically the Native Vegetation Protection Law (Lei n° 12.651/2012), which requires effective strategies for environmental compliance concerning Permanent Preservation Areas (APP) and Legal Reserves (RL).

Recognizing a significant knowledge gap regarding appropriate species selection for Pampa restoration—especially in grassland ecosystems where the need for restoration has only recently been acknowledged—the authors sought to develop an initial, validated list of priority native species. The methodology involved three phases: 1) Compilation and systematization of native species, including information on their potential use (e.g., forage); 2) Evaluation and validation by specialists during a technical workshop; and 3) Definition and adjustment of vegetation physiognomies.

The species were categorized into three broad formations: Campestres (including dry fields, wet fields, and swamps), Florestais, and Savanoides. Crucially relevant to the thesis, the text defines **Formações Savanoides** as characterized by woody species (trees and/or shrubs) overlying a continuous herbaceous layer. This category includes 'parques de espinilho', formations explicitly characterized by the presence of **espinilho (*Vachellia caven*)** and *inhanduvá* (*Propsopis affinis*).

Conclusions

The provided text contains the introduction and methodology but not the concluding section of the document. The immediate implication and goal, however, are clearly defined: to provide essential, science-based guidance for ecological restoration in the Pampa Biome.

By compiling and validating this initial list of 181 priority native species, categorized according to their natural formations (including 'parques de espinilho'), the document aims to equip public policy managers, technicians, and farmers with the necessary tools to implement effective restoration techniques. This is necessary because successful restoration requires the introduction of species that are regionally typical and adapted to the specific environment being restored, a need which had previously been unmet in the Pampa, especially concerning native grasslands.

  • "O avanço das culturas sobre áreas de vegetação nativa, a intensificação do manejo ou da exploração nos ecossistemas nativos e a invasão por espécies exóticas, como o capim-annoni (Eragrostis plana) e o pínus, em ambientes naturais, [...] representam desafios à conservação da biodiversidade e à preservação de serviços ecossistêmicos."

Supports Ecological Role and Nurse EffectsConservation and Restoration StrategiesWoody Encroachment Dynamics

Acacia caven nurses endemic sclerophyllous trees along a successional pathway from silvopastoral savanna to forest

Root-Bernstein, M., Valenzuela, R., Huerta, M., Armesto, J., & Jaksic, F. (2017)

Abstract

The successional pathways linking the Acacia caven-dominated savanna habitat “espinal” and the closed sclerophyllous forest of central Chile have long been debated. Previously, espinal was considered an invasive degradation of closed forest that tended toward desertiﬁcation, could not be restored to forest, and had little ecological value. Recent GIS (Geographical Information System) research on land-use change has, however, detected apparent regeneration of sclerophyllous forest from espinal. This suggests that there is a successional path linking espinal and sclerophyllous forest. Here, we used surveys of transects in espinals and espinal–sclerophyllous forest transitions to ask whether (1) A. caven is an invasive spe-cies or a pioneer species, (2) forest regenerates by sclerophyllous trees “ﬁlling in” spaces between A. caven individuals, and then shading them out (plant–plant competition), or (3) forest regenerates by plant–plant facilitation between A. caven and other species, and (4) how current and historical management and condi-tion affect these potential successional mechanisms. We ﬁnd that A. caven establishes primarily in full sun-light and is unlikely to degrade forests via invasion. We also ﬁnd, for the ﬁrst time, evidence that A. caven is a nurse tree to several sclerophyllous forest tree-beneﬁciary species. Measurements of the under-canopy microhabitat of A. caven, compared to Lithraea caustica, another possible nurse species, suggest that it pro-vides a balance between shade and soil moisture retention, making it a regeneration site not only for direc-ted bird-dispersed seeds but also for undirected wind-dispersed ones. Conservation and restoration of espinals, especially in drier areas, could provide capacity for future dynamic successional pathways in cen-tral Chile.

Main Points

The study utilized field surveys across 27 transects in seven sites in central Chile, specifically sampling *Acacia caven*-dominated espinals and transitional zones leading to sclerophyllous forests. For 859 trees over 40 cm tall, researchers recorded species, size metrics (height, base diameter, canopy radius), location, and critically, instances of one tree establishing under the canopy of another to detect facilitation mechanisms. They also characterized the under-canopy microhabitat of *A. caven* (and *Lithraea caustica*) by measuring light and soil characteristics, and gathered historical land-use data from managers and owners.

The results decisively address the prevailing narrative, finding that *A. caven* establishment is consistent with a pioneer species, primarily establishing in full sunlight, and thus is "unlikely to degrade forests via invasion." The most significant finding is the documented evidence that *A. caven* functions as a nurse tree, facilitating the establishment of several sclerophyllous forest tree species. Microhabitat data supported this facilitative role: the under-canopy environment of *A. caven* provides a beneficial microclimate, offering a critical "balance between shade and soil moisture retention." This improved microsite condition aids the establishment of both bird-dispersed and wind-dispersed seeds, supporting the successional pathway through facilitation rather than competition.

Conclusions

The study successfully reframed the ecological role of the *Acacia caven*-dominated espinal. It rejected the long-held viewpoint that espinal represents an irreversible, degraded ecological state resulting from anthropogenic disturbance.

Instead, the authors conclude that espinal functions as a pioneer successional stage following degradation or disturbance. The demonstrated role of *A. caven* as a nurse tree—improving microhabitat conditions like shade and soil moisture—proves a clear successional mechanism (plant–plant facilitation) linking the open espinal savanna to the closed sclerophyllous forest. This finding contradicts the competition hypothesis (where sclerophyllous trees merely shade out *A. caven*).

In terms of practical application, the authors conclude that conservation and restoration efforts must recognize and utilize the successional capacity of *A. caven*. They propose that actively conserving espinals, especially in arid areas, is vital because these formations provide the necessary capacity and foundation for future dynamic successional pathways and ecosystem recovery in central Chile.

O EXÓTICO E SINGULAR ECOSSISTEMA DO PARQUE ESTADUAL DO ESPINILHO

Elaine Regina Oliveira dos Santos (1986)

Abstract

Situado no município de Uruguaiana, numa região cuja cobertura vegetal e predominantemente campestre, o Parque Estadual do Espinilho se distingue da paisagem da Campanha rio-grandense, devido ã sua formação florística morfologicamente similar a do bioma da savana africana. Essa singularidade paisagística, absolutamente definida e limitada no território nacional ao extremo oeste gaúcho, inspirou uma série de indagações pertinentes à sua procedência, fixação e desenvolvimento. Com o objetivo de ampliar as perspectivas de diagnóstico desse ecossistema "sui generis", foram realizados estudos da ecodinâmica da sua área. Tais estudos igualmente visam contribuir, mediante um enfoque geográfico, para a identificação, destaque e divulgação da importância ecológica desse Parque Estadual, que atualmente persistE ameaçado de extinção.

Main Points

The study analyzes the unique 276-hectare Espinilho State Park in Uruguaiana, RS, Brazil, which exhibits a park-type vegetation distinct from the surrounding Campanha (Pampas) grasslands. This unique structure is defined primarily by the association of arboreal legumes: *Prosopis* species (algarrobo and inhanduvá) and *Acacia caven* (espinilho).

Investigation into the ecosystem's origin suggests that the flora is a relict population, originating from invasions of arboreal legumes from the Argentine Mesopotamian Park during a past, drier phase of the Quaternary period, reinforcing its paleoclimatic heritage.

The persistence of this xerophilous vegetation in a predominantly humid climatic region (RS) is explained by local natural conditions. The species exhibit significant adaptations—small, deciduous leaves, spines, thick bark, and deep, horizontally extensive root systems—designed to minimize water loss and cope with high thermal and pluviometric variability, coupled with specific, problematic edaphic conditions (shallow, poorly drained soils with expansive clays that hinder water storage).

Ecologically, the park provides crucial habitat for avifauna; several bird species, including *Anumbius annumbi*, *Coryphistera alaudina*, and *Picoides mixtus*, limit their known occurrence and nesting areas within Brazilian territory exclusively to the Espinilho Park.

Conclusions

The author concludes that the legal creation of the park (Decree 23.798/75) has failed to ensure its survival due to a lack of effective implementation measures, resources, and institutional will. The park lands remain under private ownership and are actively exploited. Exploitation includes the construction of dikes for irrigation, leading to gradual deforestation of the arboreal legumes and advancement of rice cultivation (*rizicultura*) and cattle grazing (*pecuária*) into the preserve.

Crucially, the greatest current threats are posed not just by local landowners but by governmental infrastructure projects, specifically proposed dams along the Uruguay River. The author stresses that governmental bodies (Municipal, State, or Federal) have a responsibility to the national natural heritage. Any spatial modification, particularly those affecting established Permanent Preservation Areas, must undergo prior technical assessment and public consultation to address the inevitable ecological and socioeconomic consequences. These impacts include the destruction of ancient ecological niches, the forcing of rural populations into displacement (exodus), and widespread political and economic destabilization.

The paper ultimately argues that the existence of protected areas often serves primarily as a mechanism for channeling financial resources to public administration organs, whose commitment to conservation is questionable given the progressive and unpunished degradation of these permanent preservation areas throughout Rio Grande do Sul.

Supports Woody Encroachment DynamicsGrazing and Land Use ImpactsConservation and Restoration Strategies

Woody plant encroachment pervasive across three socially and ecologically diverse ecoregions

Londe, D. W., S. M. Cady, R. D. Elmore, and S. D. Fuhlendorf. (2022)

Abstract

Woody plant encroachment in grasslands represents one of the greatest challenges for global biodiversity conservation. Furthermore, this is a social-ecological problem, where human activity and behavior have resulted in significant changes in ecological processes that control woody plants, and failure to fully recognize the role of human activity has led to continued loss of grasslands worldwide. It is therefore critical that conservation professionals understand how ecological systems, settlement patterns, and fragmentation from anthropogenic development interact to influence rates of woody plant encroachment. Using annual estimates of tree cover derived from regionally available remote-sensing data, our objectives were, first, to describe rates of woody plant encroachment over the last 20 years (2000–2019) across three ecologically and socially diverse ecoregions in the Southern Great Plains of North America. Then, we examined how anthropogenic and biophysical variables influenced rates of encroachment (both directly and indirectly) within the region. Results indicate that, despite marked differences in social and ecological characteristics, all three ecoregions have experienced consistent increases in woody plant encroachment during the study period. This included the Flint Hills ecoregion of Kansas and Oklahoma, an area that experiences widespread and frequent fires. At the regional scale, rates of encroachment were directly and negatively related to the average area burned in a county, initial cover of trees, and fragmentation from row crops. Percent cover of development and row crop agriculture also indirectly alter rates of encroachment in a county by influencing initial tree cover and fire activity. The pervasive nature of woody plant encroachment, even in regions that experience frequent fires, suggests that many grasslands are being managed outside of critical ecological thresholds needed to maintain grasslands and limit woody encroachment, which can have significant implications for biodiversity. Our results show that anthropogenic or ecological factors do not act in isolation in their influence on woody plant encroachment and can form complex relationships that shape regional trends in woody plant encroachment.

Main Points

The study analyzed the rate and drivers of woody plant encroachment (WPE) from 2000 to 2019 across three diverse ecoregions in the Southern Great Plains (Edwards Plateau, Flint Hills, Rolling Red Hills) using annual remote-sensing data (Rangeland Analysis Platform) aggregated at the county level. The researchers calculated the average annual rate of tree cover change using simple linear regression for each county.

To identify causal relationships, structural equation models (SEM) were developed using county-level anthropogenic variables (population density, land cover of agriculture/development, road density) and biophysical variables (initial tree cover, precipitation, average area burned). These models tested the hypothesis that broad socioeconomic patterns favoring frequent fire would limit encroachment.

Results confirmed that WPE was pervasive, showing consistent increases in woody plant cover across all three ecoregions, even in the historically fire-managed Flint Hills. At the regional scale, SEM revealed direct and negative relationships between the rate of encroachment and the average area burned, initial tree cover, and fragmentation from row crops. Furthermore, the analysis highlighted critical indirect effects: percent cover of development and row crop agriculture indirectly accelerated WPE by influencing initial tree cover and reducing fire activity within a county. This demonstrated that WPE is driven by complex interactions rather than isolated factors.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the pervasive nature of woody plant encroachment throughout the Southern Great Plains, even in fire-adapted regions, indicates that grasslands are frequently being managed outside the critical ecological thresholds required for their maintenance. This management failure carries significant consequences for global biodiversity and resilience.

The central conclusion reinforces the paradigm that WPE is fundamentally a social-ecological problem. The study provides a necessary framework for understanding the complex causal relationships between human activity (e.g., settlement patterns, fragmentation) and ecological processes (e.g., fire regimes). The research explicitly demonstrates that anthropogenic and ecological factors interact in complex ways to shape regional WPE trends, rather than acting independently. Ultimately, the findings urge conservation professionals to recognize the interconnected role of human activity and landscape structure as the primary drivers, thereby guiding more effective, regional-scale conservation strategies aimed at limiting woody encroachment.

  • "Furthermore, this is a social-ecological problem, where human activity and behavior have resulted in significant changes in ecological processes that control woody plants, and failure to fully recognize the role of human activity has led to continued loss of grasslands worldwide."
  • "It is therefore critical that conservation professionals understand how ecological systems, settlement patterns, and fragmentation from anthropogenic development interact to influence rates of woody plant encroachment."
  • "The pervasive nature of woody plant encroachment, even in regions that experience frequent fires, suggests that many grasslands are being managed outside of critical ecological thresholds needed to maintain grasslands and limit woody encroachment, which can have significant implications for biodiversity."
  • "Our results show that anthropogenic or ecological factors do not act in isolation in their influence on woody plant encroachment and can form complex relationships that shape regional trends in woody plant encroachment."
  • "This regime shift, termed woody plant encroachment, is a global challenge affecting grasslands and savannahs across multiple continents..."
  • "Woody plant encroachment has been partly attributed to widespread suppression of fire by humans, which has allowed disturbance-sensitive tree species to increase in coverage and extent in remaining grasslands..."
  • "An emerging paradigm in grassland conservation is the shift toward understanding that woody plant encroachment in grasslands is a social-ecological problem (Donovan et al. 2018, Luvuno et al. 2018, Wilcox et al. 2018)."

  • "Other factors relating to human activity such as settlement patterns, alternative land uses, and intensity of fragmentation can further influence tree encroachment by creating refuges where trees can become established or by altering disturbance patterns, such as fire and grazing, that would have otherwise limited encroachment..."
Supports Grazing and Land Use ImpactsConservation and Restoration StrategiesEcological Role and Nurse Effects

Building alliances and consensus around social-ecological rewilding in Chile

Meredith Root-Bernstein and Matı´as Guerrero-Gatica (2024)

Abstract

We provide a case study of how we position our rewilding project in central Chile in order to ﬁnd scientiﬁc and social support and build alliances, collaborations, and consensus. Our core vision focuses on reintroducing guanacos (Lama guanicoe) to central Chile in order to provide natural restoration and ecosystem processes in espinal woodlands dominated by the native tree Vachellia [Acacia] caven. We envision a scenario of “social-ecological rewilding” with widespread guanaco browsing in woodlands and guanaco migration across the region, coexisting with multiple human uses of the landscape. Guanacos would ideally be managed by regional collectives who could beneﬁt from guanaco tourism, sustainable harvest of their ﬁber (wool), and regulated hunting. Our wider vision for reintroductions and integrated conservation management extends to a set of other species that may have coexisted with guanacos and V. caven at various points in the past, but more research is necessary to establish and gain support for evidence-based baselines. Our strategy is to inspire actors with greater resources (land, money, inﬂuence) to share our vision and implement it, in collaboration with the NGO that we have formed to support our projects. Over ten years, circulating alternate interpretations and a novel imaginary of how central Chile was in the past and could be in the future, along with developing and testing scientiﬁc hypotheses, has moved our vision from an idea shared by two people to one that a wide variety of actors publicly embrace.

Main Points

The authors detail a multi-phase strategy for implementing social-ecological rewilding in central Chile, specifically focusing on reintroducing guanacos (*Lama guanicoe*) to restore ecosystem processes in *Vachellia caven* espinal woodlands. The project began in 2014 and evolved through experimental work and social alliance building.

The first phase (2014–2016) was a naturalistic experiment confirming that guanacos spontaneously browse *V. caven*, which responds with compensatory growth—a finding that supports the initial hypothesis that this tree's growth pattern is an adaptation to browsing. This scientific finding is crucial as it leverages previous work showing that coppicing and pruning of the espino results in positive ecological outcomes, such as increased tree canopy and agricultural productivity. Subsequent phases involved the practical and regulatory challenges of releasing the experimental animals into a private nature sanctuary (Phase 2, 2017) and establishing a breeding and rehabilitation center (Phase 3, 2019–present).

Social strategy and results are central to the paper. The authors actively built consensus by organizing scientific symposiums and collaborating with various stakeholders, including conservation NGOs (like WCS Chile), academic researchers, private landowners, and public officials. This effort culminated in a broader vision (Phase 4, envisioned) to create a large corridor for guanaco migration and active release east of Santiago, combining conservation goals with local economic benefits (e.g., guanaco tourism and fiber harvest). The overall approach, described as circulating "alternate interpretations and a novel imaginary" of the region's past, has successfully transformed the project from an idea shared by two individuals into a widely supported regional initiative.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that successful ecological restoration, particularly rewilding, must adopt a social-ecological framework that actively seeks coexistence between nature restoration and sustainable human use. They argue that rewilding, which aims to restore keystone processes through species reintroduction (like guanaco browsing), is compatible with human interactions and resource use, challenging the common conservation belief that environmental management must be 'anti-cattle and anti-resource use.'

They highlight a significant gap in Chilean conservation, noting that many private landholders and environmentalists assume traditional practices like non-intensive cattle grazing and timber resource use are negative, often lacking local empirical evidence. Conversely, the authors hypothesize that the historical removal of native large browsers, followed by the contemporary regulatory reduction of traditional cattle/horse grazing and activities like leaf raking, may actually *contribute* to negative environmental outcomes, such as increasing the intensity of wildfires. Therefore, the rewilding strategy is inherently social: it aims to integrate the restored ecological processes (guanaco presence) into regional collectives that derive tangible economic and cultural benefits, ensuring the project's long-term viability and social acceptance by aligning conservation with diversified rural livelihoods.

  • "Extant camelids and deer are extirpated from most of central Chile, although these have been ecologically replaced to some degree by free-range cattle, horses, and sheep."
  • "Central Chile has long been regarded as degraded, in ways that are intertwined with the history of land reform, rural development and a neoliberal economic approach."
  • "it is concerning to us that the majority consider appropriately pro-environmental management to be anti-cattle and anti-resource use, in the absence of any local empirical studies to back up this conclusion."
  • "In central Chile, cattle are typically kept not for market-oriented production, at low densities with little human contact, practically in the same way as rewilded cattle in Europe, as a traditional practice with symbolic cultural importance."
  • "The ecological impacts of all of these activities (except honey production) are assumed to be negative but have not been studied."
  • "We hypothesize that, in the absence of any large native browsers or soil disturbers, the reduction of cattle and horse grazing by exclusion, and the reduction via regulation of leaf raking, may together contribute to increasing the intensity of wild ﬁres, which is a serious and increasing problem in central Chile."

Supports Grazing and Land Use ImpactsWoody Encroachment DynamicsPampas Ecosystem Degradation and Resilience

The complex interaction between megaherbivores, climate and ﬁre has shaped the evolution and distribution of plant spinescence across biogeographical realms

Rachel Souza Ferreira, Jens J. Ringelberg, Colin Hughes, Eduardo Arlé, Friederike J. R. Wölke, Kyle W. Tomlinson, Renske E. Onstein (2025)

Abstract

The evolutionary arms race between plants and herbivores has led to numerous plant adaptations, including spinescence. However, whether spinescence evolved primarily in response to herbivory, or whether abiotic conditions also played a role, remains unknown. We integrated phylogenetic, geographic, and trait data for 2,686 species of an ecologically diverse and spiny pantropical lineage – mimosoid legumes – with data for 235 extant and 185 extinct mammalian herbivores >10 kg. Using structural equation models, we assessed how herbivores, climate and fire directly and indirectly affected the proportion of spinescent mimosoids across global and continental assemblages. The proportion of spinescent mimosoids in assemblages increased with extant and extinct herbivore richness, drought and heat, while fire influenced spinescence indirectly, by affecting herbivore richness. Notably, correlations of spinescence differed between Africa and America, with increasing importance of extinct herbivores in Africa, illustrating legacy effects on spinescence. Megaherbivores have shaped spinescence in mimosoids, especially in dry environments, where losing plant tissues is costly. Spinescence originated ~35 Mya, with the transition of mimosoids to seasonally dry environments, pre-dating the Miocene expansion of savannas. Our study suggests that both long-term climatic transitions and the emergence of open, herbivore-rich landscapes played crucial roles in the evolution and distribution of spinescence.

Main Points

The study established a comprehensive comparative framework to analyze the drivers of spinescence evolution and distribution across the global tropics, focusing on mimosoid legumes (Tribe Mimoseae), a pantropical clade including many spiny species. The authors compiled spinescence trait data for 2,686 mimosoid species (76.7% of the total) and combined this with species distribution data and a time-calibrated phylogeny, analyzing data across a global grid with approximately 100 km resolution.

Key variables quantified included the proportion of spinescent mimosoid species, species richness of extant and extinct medium- to large-sized mammalian herbivores (>10 kg), average bioclimatic variables (drought, heat), and fire frequency. Structural Equation Models (SEMs) were utilized to assess the complex direct and indirect relationships between these variables across global and continental assemblages (specifically comparing Africa and America).

The main results demonstrated that the proportion of spinescent mimosoids in a given assemblage increased significantly with both extant and extinct megaherbivore richness. Spinescence also positively correlated directly with abiotic conditions, specifically drought and heat, highlighting that defense is particularly advantageous in environments where tissue loss is costly. Fire, however, did not show a direct influence on spinescence but acted indirectly by affecting herbivore richness. A crucial finding was the evidence for continental differences, suggesting that legacy effects are vital, particularly noting the severe megafauna extinctions experienced by the Americas during the Pleistocene.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that megaherbivores have fundamentally shaped the evolution and distribution of plant spinescence in mimosoids, particularly in seasonally dry environments. The study provides strong evidence that spinescence is the result of a complex interplay between megaherbivory, climate, and fire history, contradicting explanations focusing solely on contemporary pressures.

The research indicates that spinescence is an evolutionarily deep trait, originating approximately 35 million years ago, coinciding with the transition of mimosoids into seasonally dry environments, a period preceding the major expansion of global savannas. This deep history, combined with continental comparisons, suggests that spinescence can be considered an 'evolutionary anachronism' in areas that suffered severe megafauna extinction, such as parts of the Americas. Specifically, the legacy effects of extinct megaherbivores are necessary to fully explain the current distribution of spiny plants in regions now relatively poor in large herbivores. Thus, the final conclusion is that the distribution of these defense traits is shaped by a combination of long-term climatic transitions and the historical presence of open, herbivore-rich landscapes.

  • "Megaherbivores have shaped spinescence in mimosoids, especially in dry environments, where losing plant tissues is costly."

  • "Second, extinct herbivores may have left an imprint (‘legacy effect’) on the distribution of spinescence in ecosystems today."
  • "Spinescence in these systems may thus represent adaptations to browsing by now extinct megaherbivores, making them evolutionary anachronisms (Janis, 2002)."
  • "The drivers of the origin, diversification, and distribution of defense traits and spinescent lineages remain unclear, but spinescence likely resulted from complex interactions between megaherbivores, climate and fire."
  • "Although South America and Africa historically had similar levels of herbivore richness (Owen-Smith, 2013), South America experienced more severe megafauna extinctions during the Pleistocene, losing approximately 80 species (38.65%) of herbivores over 10 kg..."

  • "Extinct (mega-)herbivores may be particularly important for explaining the distribution of spinescence in regions that lost most megaherbivores in the Pleistocene (i.e., the Americas), reflecting a legacy effect (Stuart, 2015)."
