o "PARQUE E8PINILHO" NA LITERATURA DE BALDUÍNO RAMBOl

José Newton Cardoso Marchiori; Fabiano da Silva Alves (2013)

Abstract

São comparados os textos de "A Fisionomia do Rio Grande do Sul" com os relatos das duas viagens de Balduíno Rambo ao sudoeste do mesmo estado, com o objetivo de elucidar equívocos cometidos pelo grande botânico em sua obra-prima. Comprova-se que o autor confunde os nomes comuns de Prosopis affinis e Vachellia caven, bem como atribui à singularidade vegetacional de Barra do Quaraí o nome equivocado de "Parque Espinilho".

Main Points

This study analyzes and compares Balduíno Rambo's seminal botanical work, *A Fisionomia do Rio Grande do Sul* (1942 and 1956 editions), with his previously unpublished field diaries detailing two expeditions (1941 and 1944/1945) to the southwestern region of Rio Grande do Sul, aiming to clarify historical botanical errors.

The research demonstrates that Rambo, in characterizing the unique, thorny vegetation of the region, confused the common names of two key Mimosoideae species: *Prosopis affinis* (the true inhanduvá/algarrobo) and *Vachellia caven* (the true espinilho). Specifically, Rambo assigned the common name "nhanduvaí" (which belongs to *P. affinis*) to the species *Vachellia caven* (misidentified taxonomically as *Acacia farnesiana*). Critically, Rambo described this species as widespread and noted its aggressive behavior, stating it was "Invading os campos, constitui... pequenos parques muito prejudiciais às pastagens" (Invading the fields, constitutes... small parks very harmful to pastures).

Conversely, Rambo applied the name "algarrobo" (which corresponds to another species, *Prosopis nigra*, not typically found there) to *Prosopis affinis*, accurately describing its unique morphology and restricted distribution in the area of Barra do Quaraí, a location he failed to fully explore before the first edition of his book. The term "Parque Espinilho," coined by Rambo and subsequently formalized in state conservation law, was incorrectly applied to this vegetation singularity dominated by *P. affinis*, when geographically and compositionally, the term should refer to the widespread *Espinillal* dominated by *V. caven*.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that Rambo's confusion regarding common names and scientific identification of *P. affinis* and *V. caven* was a fundamental error that became entrenched in the official literature and led to the creation of the *Parque Estadual do Espinilho* with a geographically and botanically misleading name.

Despite having the opportunity to correct these errors, including after his second expedition in 1944/1945 (where he visited the *P. affinis* park at Jarau), Rambo maintained the critical confusion in the revised 1956 edition, particularly the perpetuation of the name "nhanduvaí" for *Vachellia caven*.

This historical misidentification is significant because Rambo's description of *V. caven* (under the name 'nhanduvaí') explicitly frames the species as detrimental to pastoral landscapes ("muito prejudiciais às pastagens"). The maintenance of this misaligned nomenclature and the negative ecological framing by Rambo contributed to the prevailing narrative concerning woody vegetation in the Campanha/Pampas region.

Key Quotes

  • "Comprova-se que o autor confunde os nomes comuns de Prosopis affinis e Vachellia caven, bem como atribui à singularidade vegetacional de Barra do Quaraí o nome equivocado de "Parque Espinilho"."
  • "Não restam dúvidas acerca da origem do termo "Parque Espinilho", que dá nome à unidade de conservação criada pelo governo do estado do Rio Grande do Sul no município de Barra do Quaraí: cunhado por Balduíno Rambo..."
  • "Se não restam dúvidas sobre a origem do termo "Parque Espinilho", sobram indagações acerca de sua adequação à tipologia de vegetação em foco e, até mesmo, sobre a identidade botânica de suas principais espécies na obra de Balduíno Rambo..."
  • "São principalmente duas espécies de leguminosas mimosoídeas, que determinam o aspecto curioso destes parques espinhosos e sêcos: o algarrobo (Prosopis Juliflora) e o nhanduvaí (Acacia farnesiana)."
  • "O nhanduvaí é a mais espalhada. Completamente faltante nas outras partes do Estado, seus primeiros vestígios começam a se manifestar na linha que liga Bagé, Cruz Alta, barra do Ijuí, Rio Uruguai."
  • "Invadindo os campos, constitui, ainda nos trechos mais secos, pequenos parques muito prejudiciais às pastagens; às mais das vezes, porém, cresce em exemplares isolados..."
  • "Como se vê, o próprio autor, em seus comentários, não deixa margem a dúvidas sobre a identificação da espécie: para Balduíno Rambo, o nome comum "nhanduvaí" se aplica à Vachellia caven (Molina) Seigler & Ebinger, o popular "espinilho"..."
  • "A gravidade do equívoco cometido por Rambo reside, sobretudo, na atribuição do nome comum "nhanduvaí" a uma espécie do gênero Acacia (atual Vachellia), posto constar este termo... exclusivamente, tanto na literatura especializada como no linguajar regional."
  • "Na segunda edição de "A Fisionomia do Rio Grande do Sul - Ensaio de Monografia Natural", a única revista pelo autor, Balduíno Rambo corrigiu apenas aspectos de menor importância."
  • "De mais graves efeitos, cabe salientar, é a manutenção do nome comum "nhanduvaí" para Acacia farnesiana."

A VEGETAÇÃO NO PARQUE ESTADUAL DO ESPINILHO. 1- HISTÓRICO DA OCUPAÇÃO HUMANA E EVOLUÇÃO DO CONHECIMENTO BOTÂNICO E FITOGEOGRÁFICO SOBRE O PONTAL DO QUARAÍ.

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORF, FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES, LEONARDO PAZ DEBLE, ANABELA SILVEIRA DE OLIVEIRA DEBLE (2013)

Abstract

A história da ocupação humana no Pontal do Quaraí, extremo sudoeste do Rio Grande do Sul, e da evolução do conhecimento botânico e fitogeográfico sobre a vegetação do Parque Estadual do Espinilho, são presentemente investigados, com vistas a contribuir ao embasamento científico regional. Palavras-chave: Fitogeografia, Parque Estadual do Espinilho, Rio Grande do Sul.

Main Points

The study analyzes the history of human occupation and the development of botanical knowledge concerning the Pontal do Quaraí region (extreme southwest of Rio Grande do Sul), focusing specifically on the area now covered by the Espinilho State Park.

Two distinct economic cycles are identified. The first, extending from indigenous presence through the Jesuit missions (1626) and subsequent extensive cattle ranching (including the Estância de Japeju) until the decline of the 'Charqueada' industry in the 1930s, had a "relatively small" environmental impact. This pastoral economy relied fundamentally on the maintenance of native fields and 'parques naturais' (arboreal formations).

The second cycle began around 1937 with the rise of intensive irrigated rice agriculture (lavoura orizícola). This shift was facilitated by favorable local conditions (flat lands, abundant water from the Uruguay and Quaraí rivers, and new railway links). The text notes that this agricultural expansion led to the "drastic modification" of the landscape through the suppression of vast portions of native fields and the arboreal vegetation of the natural parks. The authors highlight that the growth of rice farming fundamentally replaced the historical agro-pastoral activities that had previously defined the region's economy.

The historical narrative establishes the context for why conservation measures were necessary: the native vegetation, including the unique formations of Inhanduvá (*Vachellia caven*) and Algarrobo, faced imminent loss. The creation of the Espinilho State Park and legal protection for Inhanduvá were crucial reactions to this intense land conversion.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the drastic transformation of the Pontal do Quaraí landscape resulted primarily from the shift from extensive cattle ranching to intensive rice cultivation starting in the late 1930s. This agricultural expansion caused the suppression of both native fields and native arboreal parks.

The review underscores the fundamental importance of the Parque Estadual do Espinilho, arguing that without its creation and the legal protection of the Inhanduvá (*Vachellia caven*), Rio Grande do Sul would likely have lost one of its "most singular natural patrimonies in the national context": the parks of Inhanduvá (Nandubaysal) and Algarrobo (Algarrobal).

Therefore, the historical analysis provides essential scientific background, emphasizing that the resilience and preservation of these unique arboreal formations, rather than their removal, is critical for regional conservation efforts.

Key Quotes

  • "A VEGETAÇÃO NO PARQUE ESTADUAL DO ESPINILHO. 1- HISTÓRICO DA OCUPAÇÃO HUMANA E EVOLUÇÃO DO CONHECIMENTO BOTÂNICO E FITOGEOGRÁFICO SOBRE O PONTAL DO QUARAÍ."
  • "Palavras-chave: Fitogeografia, Parque Estadual do Espinilho, Rio Grande do Sul."
  • "Sob o ponto de vista ambiental, o período que findava teve impacto relativamente pequeno sobre a paisagem e biota, comparado ao que estava por vir, uma vez que dependia da vegetação nativa dos campos e dos parques naturais para a atividade pastoril."
  • "O golpe fatal deu-se em 1927, com a Lei Federal de Desnacionalização do Charque, que passou a proibir o trânsito do produto para portos brasileiros, via Montevidéu."
  • "Na contramão do previsto por Veloso da Silveira, a lavoura orizícola deu início a um novo ciclo, em quadro econômico deprimido pelo ocaso da indústria do charque."
  • "As condições geográficas do Pontal do Quaraí eram excepcionalmente favoráveis à lavoura do arroz: terras planas; água em abundância, graças aos rios Uruguai e Quaraí; solo fértil..."

  • "...os parques de inhanduvá (Nandubaysal) e de algarrobo (Algarrobal), preservados na referida unidade de conservação."
  • "Ao tratar da evolução do conhecimento botânico e fitogeográfico no Pontal do Quaraí e da história da ocupação humana na região, busca-se, justamente, um novo olhar sobre estes temas, bem como contribuir para o embasamento científico da vegetação no espaço regional."
Neutral Woody Encroachment DynamicsPampas Ecosystem Degradation and ResilienceGrazing and Land Use Impacts

A VEGETAÇÃO DO PARQUE ESTADUAL DO ESPINILHO. 2 - ORIGEM DO NOME E CONSIDERAÇÕES FITOGEOGRÁFICAS

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI, FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES, LEONARDO PAZ DEBLE, ANABELA SILVEIRA DE OLIVEIRA DEBLE (2014)

Abstract

A origem do nome e as tipologias de vegetação reconhecidas no Parque Estadual do Espinilho (Rio Grande do Sul, Brasil) são presentemente investigadas, com vistas ao esclarecimento de questões fitogeográficas pendentes na literatura.

Main Points

The central objective of this article is to analyze the origin of the official name of the Espinilho State Park and describe the existing vegetation typologies, addressing phytogeographical inaccuracies prevalent in the literature. The authors meticulously trace the origin of the name 'Parque Espinilho' back to Balduíno Rambo (1942), who was influenced by Lindman (1906).

Key to the discussion is the historical confusion surrounding the identity of two major Chacoan trees. Rambo, during a brief 1941 visit to Barra do Quaraí, mistakenly identified *Vachellia caven* (the true 'espinilho') as 'nhandu vaí' and *Prosopis affinis* (the true 'inhanduvá') as 'algarrobo.' Although Rambo later corrected these common names in a 1946 report, the original confusing binomials persisted in his influential work, leading to the misleading designation of the park.

The authors differentiate between two distinct silvático-campestres typologies:
1. **Parque de Inhanduvá (or Nandubaysal):** Found in Barra do Quaraí (the location of the state park), characterized by the dominance of *Prosopis affinis* and *Vachellia caven*, typically associated with localized sandy/sedimentary formations.
2. **Parque de Espinilhos (or Espinillal):** Dominated essentially by *Vachellia caven* alone. The authors note that these 'true' *Parques de Espinilhos* are widespread across the Campanha and other central regions of Rio Grande do Sul because *V. caven* is not linked to specific sedimentary formations, unlike *P. affinis*.

Conclusions

The article concludes that the official designation 'Parque Estadual do Espinilho' is inadequate and results from a historical error and 'careless reading' of Balduíno Rambo's foundational work. Rambo, despite being the most important botanist in the region, failed to adequately revise his text to correct the initial misidentification of *Vachellia caven* and *Prosopis affinis* nomenclature.

The official name is deemed inappropriate because the vegetation singularity of the conservation unit in Barra do Quaraí is defined by the prevalence of *Prosopis affinis* (inhanduvá). Therefore, the park should more accurately be named 'Parque de Inhanduvá,' a suggestion previously championed by other researchers. The designation 'Parque Espinilho' inaccurately applies a name strictly corresponding to *V. caven*-dominated areas (Espinillares), which, although widespread, do not characterize the unique ecological structure that the conservation unit was established to protect. The article highlights how this flawed nomenclature inadvertently enshrines a scientific error.

A NEW COMBINATION IN VACHELLIA WIGHT & ARN. (MIMOSACEAE)

LEONARDO PAZ DEBLE, JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI (2009)

Abstract

Acacia ibirocayensis Marchiori, species endemic in southwest of Rio Grande do Sul state (Brazil) is transferred illustration, comments about geographic distribution, conservation and allied to genus Vachellia. Description, taxa are furnished. Key words: Vachellia, Acacia, Mimosaceae, Taxonomy, Rio Grande do Sul, Brazil.

Main Points

The primary objective was to formally transfer the endemic Brazilian species *Acacia ibirocayensis* into the genus *Vachellia*, necessitated by the rehabilitation and widespread acceptance of *Vachellia* as a distinct genus separate from *Acacia* s. l. (following Seigler & Ebinger, 2006).

**Results:** The authors established the new combination: *Vachellia ibirocayensis* (Marchiori) Deble & Marchiori, comb. novo. A detailed morphological description was provided, noting that it is a subshrub 1–2 m high with stout stipular spines, solitary globose capitula (9–11 mm diameter), and linear-elliptic to linear-oblong legumes (5–7 cm long).

**Differentiation and Distribution:** The species was compared to allied taxa. It differs from *V. astringens* (which is a larger shrub/tree, 4–12 m tall, with clustered capitula) and from *V. farnesiana* (which usually has clustered capitula and different legume morphology). Geographically, *V. ibirocayensis* is likely endemic to the southwest of Rio Grande do Sul (Brazil), restricted to stony grasslands and ravines near the Ibirocai rivers.

**Conservation:** The authors noted that the species' populations are highly fragmented and contain few individuals. Given its reduced area of occurrence, rarity, and observed threats, the authors formally recommended that *V. ibirocayensis* be classified as **Critically Endangered (CR)** under IUCN criteria (CR B 1a,b (i,ii,iii,iv), C2a(i)).

Conclusions

The paper successfully established the new taxonomic status for the species, acknowledging the modern phylogenetic understanding that separates *Vachellia* from *Acacia*. The most significant conclusion relates to conservation: *Vachellia ibirocayensis* is confirmed to be an extremely rare endemic species within the Rio Grande do Sul state, currently existing in fragmented populations.

Based on these findings regarding its rarity, geographic restriction, and fragmentation, the authors strongly concluded that the species warrants immediate placement in the Critically Endangered category on the IUCN Red List. This highlights the severe threat facing this specific *Vachellia* species within the Southern Brazilian ecosystem, emphasizing the fragility of its habitat (stony grasslands and ravines) within a region characterized by intense land use pressures.

ANATOMIA DA MADEIRA DE VACHELLIA FARNESIANA (L.) WIGHT & ARN.I

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORF (2010)

Abstract

A madeira de Vachelliafarnesiana (L.) Wight & Arn. é anatomicamente descrita, com base em amostras procedentes do Rio Grande do Sul. A estrutura anatômica assemelha-se ao descrito para Vachelia caven e V ibirocayensis, aliando fibras não septadas e de paredes espessas, contrastantes com o parênquima axial, a séries parenquimáticas de 2, raro 3 células. A identificação de Vachellia farnesiana requer o exame de caracteres quantitativos, salientando-se o comprimento de elementos vasculares, o diâmetro dos cristais no parênquima axial e a freqüência de raios. Palavras-chave: Vachelliafarnesiana, Acaciafarnesiana, Fabaceae, Leguminosae Mimosoideae, anatomia da madeira.

Main Points

The study aims to describe the general, macroscopic, and microscopic characteristics of *Vachellia farnesiana* wood and compare its anatomy with related species, specifically *Vachellia caven* and *V. ibirocayensis*.

### Methods
The material consisted of two cultivated wood samples collected in Santa Maria and Jaguari, Rio Grande do Sul (RS), Brazil. The samples were prepared for microtome sectioning (20 µm thickness) in three anatomical planes (transversal, radial, tangential) and for maceration using the Jeffrey method. Sections were stained using acridina-vermelha, crisoidina, and azul-de-astra, and anatomical descriptions followed COPANT (1973) standards. Measurements were taken for quantitative features like vessel frequency, diameter, element length, ray frequency, and fiber length.

### Results
Macroscopically, the wood is hard, very heavy (1.04 g/cm³), with distinct, reddish-brown heartwood and yellowish sapwood, possessing good natural durability. The axial parenchyma is visible to the naked eye, abundant, paratracheal, and organized in irregular, predominantly tangential bands (zoned and confluent).

Microscopically, the wood is characterized by very numerous, small vessels (17–56/mm²), mostly in radial multiples and clusters. Vessel elements are very short (average 221 µm) with simple perforation plates. Axial parenchyma is abundant (~27% of volume), typically arranged in series of 2, rarely 3 or 4 cells. Romboidal calcium oxalate crystals are notable, occurring in two sizes: small (~25 µm) and large (up to 80 µm). Rays are numerous (6–11/mm), homogeneous, and predominantly multiseriate (often greater than 4 cells wide). Fibers are libriform, non-septate, short (average 953 µm), and thin-walled (~3.4 µm). The anatomical structure closely resembles *V. caven* and *V. ibirocayensis*.

Conclusions

The study concludes that the presence of non-septate, thick-walled fibers combined with abundant, contrastingly thin-walled axial parenchyma composed of 2 (rarely 3) cell series constitutes a highly diagnostic set of anatomical features common to *Vachellia farnesiana*, *V. caven*, and *V. ibirocayensis*. This specific structure allows for easy identification of the genus *Vachellia*, distinguishing it from all other species of the former genus *Acacia* native to Rio Grande do Sul.

Quantitative analysis is necessary to differentiate among the three native species. *V. farnesiana* can be separated from *V. caven* by its longer vessel elements (221 µm vs. 167 µm) and more numerous rays (9/mm vs. 6/mm). Both species share rays that are predominantly wider than 4 cells and the presence of large romboidal crystals in the axial parenchyma (up to 80 µm).

In contrast, *V. ibirocayensis* is distinct from both *V. farnesiana* and *V. caven* due to its predominantly uniseriate rays and the presence of only small romboidal crystals (~25 µm) in the axial parenchyma.

  • "Descrita inicialmente por Linnaeus (Mimo-sa farnesiana L.), a espécie em estudo figura em importantes monografias botânicas como Acacia farnesiana (L.) Willd."
  • "Recentemente, com a segregação do gênero Acacia (Toum.) Miller e conseqüente reabilita-ção de Vachellia (Seigler & Ebinger, 2006)... O nome científico válido para a espécie passa a ser Vachellia farnesiana (L.) Wight & Am."

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 1- EMBASAMENTO FITOGEOGRÁFICO E PENDÊNCIAS TERMINOLÓGICAS.

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI, FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES (2010)

Abstract

São discutidas questões fitogeográficas e terminológicas, constantes na literatura sobre o inhanduvá (Prosopis affinis Spreng., Fabaceae) no Rio Grande do Sul.

Main Points

The study aims to establish the phytogeographical basis and resolve terminological confusions regarding *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá) and associated woody species in Rio Grande do Sul (RS), Brazil. This unique assemblage, including *Vachellia caven* (Espinilho), is categorized as “Chaquenho elements,” seen as the easternmost extension of the Argentine Pampas/Espinal, concentrated in the state's southwestern corner.

The authors confirm that the vegetation in the “Parque Estadual do Espinilho” (Barra do Quaraí) is a prolongation of the Argentine Espinal Province, specifically the Distrito del Nandubay (Inhanduvá District), part of the Chaquenho Domain. This district is characterized by various associations, including the Espinillar, dominated by *V. caven*.

Crucially, the paper highlights the threat posed by human land use. The authors note that anthropogenic action—specifically burning and cattle predation of sprouts—is detrimental to the highly valued *P. affinis*, while simultaneously favoring *Vachellia caven*. The study also dedicates significant effort to confirming that local populations historically and currently possess accurate knowledge of the common names and species distinctions (Inhanduvá, Algarrobo, Espinilho), correcting ambiguities found in older academic literature.

Conclusions

The study successfully anchors the Inhanduvá/Espinilho vegetation of Rio Grande do Sul within the well-defined phytogeographic framework of the Argentine Espinal Province (Distrito del Nandubay). This confirms the exotic, Chaquenho origin of these woody elements relative to the typical RS flora.

Furthermore, the authors conclude that despite the conservation efforts exemplified by the creation of the Espinilho Park, the integrity of the natural remnants is under continuous threat from human activity. The observed dynamic where grazing and fire disfavor the economically important *Prosopis affinis* in favor of *Vachellia caven* underscores a concerning process of ecosystem alteration and degradation. The conservation challenge lies not only in protecting the area physically but also in managing the anthropogenic pressures that shift the native woody composition, favoring the hardier, disturbance-tolerant Espinilho.

  • "O 'Parque Estadual do Espinilho', criado em 12/3/1975, visa, justamente, a preservar o fragmento mais representativo desta vegetação singular no sul do Brasil."

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 2 - OCORRÊNCIA NATURAL NA REGIÃO DO JARAU, QUARAÍ

FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI (2010)

Abstract

A distribuição geográfica do inhanduvá (Prosopis affinis Spreng., Fabaceae) no Rio Grande do Sul é presentemente estendida ao município de Quaraí, devido à comprovação de sua ocorrência natural em lente de solos arenosos próxima à encosta sul dos cerros do Jarau. Palavras-chave: Prosopis affinis, Fitogeografia, Quaraí, Rio Grande do Sul.

Main Points

The study aims to confirm and extend the known geographical distribution of *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá) in Rio Grande do Sul (RS), Brazil, specifically confirming its natural occurrence in the municipality of Quaraí, near the Jarau hills. This confirmation relies on historical documentation dating back to the early 20th century and contemporary botanical fieldwork.

Field visits in 2009 confirmed the presence of *P. affinis* in a sedimentary soil lens, approximately 5.5 km in diameter, isolated within the predominantly volcanic (meláfiro) soils typical of the Campanha Plateau. A genuine "parque de inhanduvá" was found here, containing dozens of old trees and scarce regeneration, alongside a few individuals of *Vachellia caven* (espinilhos). Notably, the herbaceous layer under the canopy lacked *Andropogon lateralis* (capim-caninha), which dominated the surrounding open grasslands, suggesting a localized modifying ecological effect by the woody vegetation.

The paper addresses significant phytogeographical controversies, particularly clarifying the historical confusion arising from Balduíno Rambo's use of popular names. The authors clarify that Rambo utilized the term "Parque Espinilho" broadly to designate various park-like vegetations, not solely the *P. affinis* and *V. caven* association found near Barra do Quaraí. They establish that the true *P. affinis* is restricted to sedimentary formations, explaining the disjunction (about 100 km) between the Quaraí population and the known Espinilho State Park population, due to the intervening unsuitable volcanic bedrock (Neossolos Regolíticos).

Conclusions

Based on the comprehensive analysis of historical documents, including Rambo's collection data from 1945, a 1925 record mentioning the Sanga Nanduvá, and a 1903 manuscript confirming *P. affinis* as the only noteworthy native timber species in Quaraí, the authors definitively conclude that *Prosopis affinis* is an autochthonous element of the Quaraí flora.

This finding significantly extends the accepted natural range of Inhanduvá, refuting the previous restrictive view that limited its occurrence exclusively to the Barra do Quaraí region (Parque Estadual do Espinilho). The disjunct distribution across the Campanha Gaúcha is attributed to specific lithopedological factors, namely the necessity for sedimentary or deep alluvial soils, which are rare amidst the widespread volcanic formations. The paper thus provides a crucial revision of the phytogeography of this important woody species in the Pampas/Campanha ecosystem, challenging the notion of its limited presence and confirming the long-term, native establishment of park-like woody formations.

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 3 - PARQUE DA CABANHA DO LORETO, SÃO VICENTE DO SUV

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI, FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES, EDUARDO ALONSO PAZ (2010)

Abstract

A ocorrência natural de inhanduvá (Prosopis affinis Spreng., Fabaceae) é presentemente estendida ao município de São Vicente do Sul (Rio Grande do Sul- Brasil), com a presente descrição de um parque existente no topo de uma colina de solos arenosos, com blocos de rochas, próxima ao rio Jaguari.

Main Points

The study aims to validate the natural occurrence of *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá) in São Vicente do Sul, Rio Grande do Sul, countering the phytogeographical view that restricts its distribution mainly to the Barra do Quaraí region (Parque Estadual do Espinilho).

The authors analyze the stand, located at Cabanha do Loreto, focusing on structural and historical evidence. The structure is described as a 'park' containing about 50 adult trees of varied height and diameter, exhibiting an inequiânea (uneven-aged) distribution, characteristic of natural vegetation. The herbaceous stratum is noted to be severely degraded due to intense cattle grazing ("pisoteio do gado"), leading to the absence of dominant native grasses and the abundance of ruderal species (indicators of intense anthropism).

The historical analysis thoroughly investigates the periods of Jesuit missions (1627–1767) and subsequent Spanish/Portuguese estância management, concluding that neither indigenous groups nor missionaries/settlers would have introduced the species. This is based on mission objectives (focused on cattle), lack of cultural records of valuing *P. affinis*, the difficulty in cultivating the slow-growing species, and the need to protect it from herbivory. Crucially, the authors note the absence of other common Chacoan elements usually associated with *P. affinis* stands, such as *Vachellia caven* (Espinilho) and *Prosopis nigra* (Algarrobo), at this specific site.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the stand of *Prosopis affinis* at Cabanha do Loreto is definitively of **natural origin** and of considerable antiquity. This conclusion is derived from the convergence of structural evidence—specifically the irregular distribution (non-standardized spacing) and the presence of very old, large individuals showing an uneven-aged structure—and the historical context, which effectively rules out human introduction during known periods of settlement or land use.

This finding significantly extends the validated natural distribution range of *P. affinis* to the center-west of Rio Grande do Sul, supporting the broader phytogeographical perspective that these thorny woody species are more widespread in the Campos Sulinos (Pampas) than some restrictive views allow. The authors implicitly reinforce the need to recognize and protect these native woody fragments, which face constant degradation from intensive land use like cattle grazing.

  • "Tema controvertido, a distribuição geográ-fica do inhanduvá (Prosopis affinis Spreng.) apresenta duas correntes divergentes na litera-tura sul-rio-grandense, havendo autores que re-ferem, para a espécie, uma área restrita aos ar-redores de Barra do Quaraí e outros que postu-lam uma distribuição mais ampla, no centro-oeste do Estado."
  • "A ocorrência natural de inhanduvá (Prosopis affinis Spreng., Fabaceae) é presentemente estendida ao muni-cípio de São Vicente do Sul (Rio Grande do Sul- Brasil), com a presente descrição de um parque existente no topo de uma colina de solos arenosos, com blocos de rochas, próxima ao rio Jaguari."

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 4 - ASPECTOS BOTÂNICO-VEGETACIONAIS E MORFOMÉTRICOS DO PARQUE DO LORETO, SÃO VICENTE DO SUV

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORF; MIGUEL ANTÃO DURL03; FABIANO DA SILVAALVES4 (2011)

Abstract

Composto por 50 indivíduos de Prosopis affinis Spreng. (Fabaceae), o parque do Loreto apresenta os inhanduvás de maior altura e diâmetro à altura do peito do Rio Grande do Sul. Outro aspecto distinto reside na copa, que varia de hernisférica até em forma de sombrinha. Palavras-chave: Prosopis affinis, Fitogeografia, Rio Grande do Sul, Dendrologia, morfometria de árvores.

Main Points

The study analyzed 50 individuals of *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá) in the Parque do Loreto, São Vicente do Sul, RS, focusing on dendrological, vegetational, and morphometric singularities. The site is located on a gentle hill with Argissolo Bruno Acinzentado soil (Acrisol) under a Cfa climate.

**Methods:** Researchers collected fertile branches for botanical confirmation and used field measurements for morphometric analysis. Key measurements included total height (H) and height to the first bifurcation (L, base of the crown) using a telescopic ruler, Diameter at Breast Height (DAP) using a diametric tape, and crown projection radii in four cardinal directions (No, Le, Sul, Oe) to calculate mean crown diameter (Dc) and area (Ac). Derived variables such as Crown Height (Hc), Crown Percentage (Pc), Crown Formal (Fc), and Trunk Slenderness Degree (GE) were calculated. Spatial positioning was determined using a 30m tape measure and GPS (Garmin Map 60 CSx). Statistical analysis employed SPSS for descriptive statistics and regression analysis (DAP vs. H; DAP vs. Ac).

**Results:** Botanically, the collected material corresponded perfectly to *P. affinis*. Morphometrically, the trees demonstrated superior dimensions compared to regional and Platine literature. Total height (H) ranged from 2.89 m to 8.5 m, with a mean of 5.20 m—significantly higher than other regional populations like the Parque Estadual do Espinilho. DAP ranged from 8.9 cm to an unprecedented 74.0 cm (mean 35.7 cm). Nine individuals exceeded 50 cm DAP. This maximum DAP far surpasses the previously accepted maximums (40–50 cm) in literature for the species in the Platine region. The crown percentage (Pc) averaged 71.70%, reaching up to 97.11%, demonstrating tall, developed crowns. Crown morphology was noted for its variability, ranging from hemispherical to umbrella-shaped, differing from the 'flattened' or 'corymbiform' standards often cited.

Conclusions

The morphological findings confirm that the *Prosopis affinis* population in Parque do Loreto is exceptional, harboring the largest and presumably longest-lived individuals in Rio Grande do Sul. The maximum recorded DAP (74.0 cm) significantly exceeds the morphological maximums cited for the species throughout the Platine literature.

Crucially, the authors interpret the trees' large size and probable advanced age as strong evidence supporting the **natural origin** of this occurrence in São Vicente do Sul. This inference is reinforced by the lack of historical documentation regarding the introduction of the species by human intervention, whether by indigenous populations or European settlers.

This study challenges the generalized descriptions of *P. affinis* often found in botanical literature, which may be based on studies of smaller, potentially younger or disturbed populations. The unique diversity in the crown structure (varying widely, especially among older trees) further highlights a broader natural fisionomic range than previously recognized. Defining these natural, maximum morphometric limits is deemed essential for future dendrological and ecological understanding of the species.

  • "...o parque de inhanduvá do Loreto também chama atenção pelas formas variadas de copa, sobretudo em indivíduos velhos, que fogem aos padrões "amplo e estendido", achatado ou corimbiforme referidos na literatura botânica para a espécie."
  • "Para os limites do Rio Grande do Sul, deste modo, pode-se afirmar que os exemplares de maior porte - e presumivelmente mais velhos - se encontram em São Vicente do Sul."
  • "No caso do Uruguai, Izaguirre & Beyhaut (2003) referem diâmetros de 30 a 40cm, para a mesma espécie."
  • "De acordo com a Tabela 2, vê-se que o DAP varia de 8,9 a 74,Ocm, com média de 35,7cm."
  • "Nenhuma das árvores medidas por Galvani alcança, sequer, a altura média observada no parque do Loreto (5,2m)."

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 5 - OCORRÊNCIA NATURAL NA VÁRZEA DO RIO SANTA MARIA, ROSÁRIO DO SUL

FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES, JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI (2011)

Abstract

A ocorrência natural de Prosopis aftinis Spreng. (Fabaceae) é estendida ao município de Rosário do Sul, Rio Grande do Sul, com a presente descrição de fragmentos remanescentes de parques de inhanduvá na planície aluvial do rio Santa Maria, uns l5km ao sul da cidade. Palavras-chave: Prosopis aftinis, Fitogeografia, Rosário do Sul, Rio Grande do Sul. | SUMMARY: [Prosopis affinis Spreng. in Rio Grande do Sul state, BraziI. 5 - Natural occurrence on Santa Maria river's flood plain, municipality of Rosario do Sul, Brazil]. The natural occurrence of Prosopis aftinis Spreng. (Fabaceae) is extended to the municipality of Rosario do Sul (Rio Grande do Sul state, Brazil), with the present description of some remaining stands on Santa Maria river's flood plain, about 15 km south from the city. Key words: Prosopis affinis, Phytogeography, municipality of Rosario do Sul, Rio Grande do Sul state, Brazil.

Main Points

The study aims to document and describe the natural occurrence of *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá), a thorny legume, in Rosário do Sul, Rio Grande do Sul, significantly extending the species' known native geographical range and challenging restrictive phytogeographical theories (e.g., those limiting occurrence solely to Barra do Quaraí).

The methodology involved field examination of residual forest fragments (known locally as 'parques de inhanduvá') on the alluvial flood plains (várzea) of the Santa Maria River. The study incorporates historical evidence, citing an early record from 1922 and local toponymy ('Fazenda Inhanduvá,' dating to 1840) to support the species' native status and long-term presence in the area, countering the view that it is restricted to the far west of the state.

Results confirm the existence of fragmented stands, mainly located on the "Fazenda Inhanduvá," characterized by high biological diversity including numerous epiphytes (Tillandsia, Pleopeltis, Oncidium) and co-occurring arboreal species. Critically, the study documents severe ecosystem degradation: the parks have been largely replaced by rice paddies ("parque que cedeu lugar a lavouras de arroz, em sua quase totalidade"). The remaining fragments, particularly those isolated in agricultural areas, are highly threatened. The physical alteration of the environment by cultivation compromises the trees' ability to survive, leading to their "morte paulatina" (gradual death). The consistent association of *P. affinis* with alluvial sediments across these new, disjunct sites reinforces their relictual nature and suggests the Ibicuí river valley as a historic migratory route.

Conclusions

The confirmation of *Prosopis affinis* in Rosário do Sul considerably expands the species' distribution in Rio Grande do Sul, reinforcing the argument against restrictive narratives regarding its native range. This extension provides crucial data for understanding the biogeography of the Espinhal Province. The authors assert that the natural origin of these stands is undeniable, supported by historical records dating back to 1922 and local oral tradition, validating the species' endemic role.

The findings highlight that these stands possess a relictual character, strongly associated with alluvial sedimentary formations. This pattern of disjunct occurrence, far east of previously acknowledged limits, points toward the Ibicuí river basin as a significant dispersal corridor from the western region of the state.

Ultimately, the study serves as a documentation of significant ecosystem degradation caused by intensive land use. The authors stress that agricultural expansion, specifically rice farming, has nearly annihilated these natural parks. The remaining fragments are acutely endangered, as soil cultivation fundamentally alters the ecological conditions necessary for the trees' survival. The research underscores the urgent need to recognize and conserve these 'true natural parks' of Inhanduvá, crucial components of the regional ecology currently being lost due to human activity.

  • "Apesar da exaustiva pesquisa bibliográfica... apenas uma referência encontrou-se sobre esta valiosa árvore no município de Rosário do Sul. Trata-se de uma breve citação, datada de 1922..."

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 6 - DESCRIÇÃO DE UM PARQUE NATURAL NA VÁRZEA DO RIO IBICUÍ, MUNICÍPIO DE CACEQUI

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI; FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES (2011)

Abstract

É descrito um parque natural de inhanduvá (Prosopis affinis Spreng.) existente na planície de inundação do rio Ibicuí, município de Cacequi. A presente ocorrência, em área disjunta, reforça a interpretação da planície adjacente ao rio Ibicuí como rota imigratória para a espécie. Palavras-chave: Prosopis affinis, Fitogeografia, município de Cacequi, Rio Grande do Sul.

Main Points

The study describes the sixth natural stand of *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá) identified in Rio Grande do Sul (RS), located on the floodplain of the Ibicuí river in the municipality of Cacequi, known as Fazenda Santa Fé. Geographically, the park is long (c. 1500m) and narrow (50 to 300m), situated at 86m altitude, and isolated from the river by small lakes and ciliar forest remnants. The terrain is sedimentary, composed of alluvial deposits, classified as Planossolo Háplico Eutrófico Arênico, common to floodplains.

Floristically, the stand contains large-sized *P. affinis* individuals, along with a rich assemblage of species derived from the adjacent riparian forest, including various trees (*Sebastiania commersoniana*, *Coccoloba brasiliensis*), lianas, and abundant epiphytes (notably *Cereus hildmannianus* and several *Tillandsia* species). The stand showed higher floristic diversity (arboreal species, epiphytes, lianas, hemiparasitas) compared to the previously studied várzea of the Santa Maria River. Importantly, it lacked classic Chaco elements (e.g., *Prosopis nigra*, *Aspidosperma quebrachoblanco*), distinguishing it from stands closer to the extreme west of RS.

The discovery of this new, disjunct park, alongside others previously described (Jarau, Loreto, Santa Maria River), is presented as definitive evidence refuting outdated bibliographic limitations that confined *P. affinis* distribution solely to the area around the Parque Estadual do Espinilho. This occurrence strongly supports the hypothesis that the sedimentary floodplains of the Ibicuí river function as a key immigratory route for the species, allowing its expansion into the interior of the state by circumventing the Planalto da Campanha.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the vegetation represents a genuine natural stand of Inhanduvá, characterized by spontaneous formation and lack of regular spacing. They detail the key ecological process at play: *Prosopis affinis* acts as a **pioneer tree** (*árvore pioneira*), facilitating the recruitment and growth of ciliar forest species (like *angico*). As these taller species grow, the resulting shading compromises the survival of *P. affinis* individuals within the park's interior structure, leading to their localized disappearance.

However, this dynamic process ensures the species' persistence, as *P. affinis* simultaneously colonizes adjacent fields under favorable edaphic conditions (Figure 2B). This spatial shift confirms the species' reliance on dynamic pioneer conditions. The primary threat identified to this ecological stability is the potential conversion of the adjacent floodplain várzea for agricultural use, specifically rice cultivation. To guarantee the preservation of the species and its associated dynamic process, the authors issue a formal recommendation that a strip of land adjacent to the park should be protected from agricultural utilization. Finally, the finding reiterates that the Ibicuí river valley, due to its unique geomorphology as a sedimentary pathway, served as the essential immigratory route for the species across the region.

Key Quotes

  • "Com a descrição dos parques de inhanduvá... não mais se sustentam, por equivocadas, as referências bibliográficas que limitavam a distribuição natural desta espécie, no Rio Grande do Sul..."
  • "o presente estudo visa a contribuir para o conhecimento da Província do Espinhal no Rio Grande do Sul, bem como reforçar a interpretação das planícies sedimentares adjacentes ao rio Ibicuí como rota imigratória da espécie em direção ao interior do Estado..."
  • "O parque reúne inhanduvás de grandes dimensões... além de espécies arbóreas oriundas da mata ciliar..."
  • "o parque em estudo difere, todavia, pela presença de espécies imigradas da mata ciliar em sua estrutura, decorrente da proximidade com o rio Ibicuí."
  • "a vegetação em estudo é um verdadeiro parque natural de inhanduvá, posto que formado, basicamente, por indivíduos de Prosopis affinis, e sem espaçamento regular."
  • "O processo dinâmico vivenciado pela espécie se pode reconhecer, muito claramente, na vegetação em estudo: como árvore pioneira, o inhanduvá favorece a entrada de espécies oriundas da mata ciliar no interior do parque..."
  • "Deste modo, os indivíduos de Prosopis affinis tendem a desaparecer no interior do parque com o crescimento de árvores mais altas, tais como o angico, conquistando espaço, todavia, no campo adjacente, desde que sob condições edáficas favoráveis."
  • "a principal ameaça ao inhanduvá reside na eventual destinação da várzea adjacente para cultivos agrícolas, notadamente o arroz."

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 7 - OCORRÊNCIA NATURAL NA PLANÍCIE DE INUNDAÇÃO DO ARROIO ITAPORORÓ, MUNICíPIO DE ALEGRETE)

FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES; JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI (2011)

Abstract

É descritoum parque naturalde inhanduváexistentenaplaníciede inundaçãodo arroioItapororó,no município de Alegrete (Rio Grande do Sul).

Main Points

The study describes and geographically locates a previously undocumented natural thicket of *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá) – a *parque de inhanduvá* – situated on the alluvial flood plain of the Itapororó stream in the municipality of Alegrete, Rio Grande do Sul. This area is characterized by sedimentary Planos solo Háplico Eutrófico Arênico and a Cfa climate.

This discovery marks the fourth such park described in the Ibicuí basin, lending substantial support to the interpretation of the Ibicuí river valley as a crucial migratory route for woody species moving into the center of Rio Grande do Sul. This finding directly challenges older phytogeographical narratives that limited the natural occurrence of Inhanduvá to the extreme southwest of the state (like the Parque Estadual do Espinilho).

The described park, although geographically isolated and small (1100m long, up to 400m wide), is confirmed to be a remnant of natural origin, hosting hundreds of mature and regenerating *P. affinis* individuals. Crucially, the vegetation assemblage includes other characteristic woody species, such as *espinilhos* (*Vachellia caven*) and *unha-de-gato* (*Senegalia bonariensis*), associating them within this natural relictual formation.

The text highlights severe anthropogenic degradation. The park is "severely threatened by rice cultivation" (*lavoura arrozeira*), resulting in numerous dead trees and partial exposure of root systems due to erosion from stream overflow. Furthermore, the abundance of *capim anoni* (*Eragrostis plana*) in the understory is cited as a "clear indication of anthropism" (*claro indício de antropismo*), linking the site degradation to intensive land use practices (likely grazing, given the indicator species).

Conclusions

The newly described *parque de inhanduvá* at Itapororó is important due to its relictual character and its strategic location in the heart of the Campanha Plateau. Although less diverse than other parks, this description reinforces the hypothesis that the Ibicuí sedimentary plain served as a critical migratory route for *Prosopis affinis* as it advanced toward the interior of Rio Grande do Sul.

The findings challenge restrictive views on the distribution of woody savanna/thicket species and prompt new discussion regarding the true geographical scope (*abrangência*) of the Espinhal Province (where *Vachellia caven* is the type species) within the State. By documenting *Vachellia caven* as a component of this severely threatened, natural relict, the study supports the narrative that these woody formations are indigenous to the Pampas interior and are being lost due to land conversion and degradation, rather than being invasive species.

PALMAR DE COATEPE (QUARAÍ, RS): ENFOQUE FITOGEOGRÁFICO

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARCHIORI; FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES (2011)

Abstract

Descrito apenas em 1995, o palmar de Coatepe é presentemente analisado sob o ponto de vista fitogeográfico e inserido no Distrito do Inhanduvá e Província do Espinhal, segundo a classificação de Cabrera & Willink. Palavras-chave: Butiá, Butia yatay, Fitogeografia, Palmar de Coatepe, Quaraí, Rio Grande do Sul.

Main Points

This paper analyzes the Coatepe Palm Grove (*Butia yatay*) in Quaraí, Rio Grande do Sul, focusing on its phytogeographical context, distribution, and conservation status. The study justifies its necessity by pointing out that previous literature often misrepresented or underestimated the true geographical distribution of *B. yatay* in the state.

Phytogeographically, the palm grove is confirmed as a natural occurrence, representing an important disjunction from the species' main distribution center in the Argentine Mesopotamia. Following Cabrera & Willink's classification, the area is inserted into the Inhanduvá District and Espinal Province, characterized by sandy-stony (areno-pedregosos) soils, which are isolated by typical volcanic rocks of the Campanha Plateau.

The Coatepe Palm Grove covers approximately 60 km², but the density of individuals is low. A critical finding is the state of the palm population: it consists primarily of mature, adult trees (4 to 8 m high), reflecting a senescent structure. The low density is attributed to the "morte paulatina dos butiás mais velhos" (gradual death of older palms) and, most importantly, the **"comprometimento da regeneração natural, exercido pelo gado"** (compromise of natural regeneration, exercised by cattle). The associated vegetation is dominated by the native grass *Elionurus sp.* in the herbaceous layer, alongside several other xeric and characteristic species, reinforcing the natural, edaphically-controlled status of the relict.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the Palmar de Coatepe is a natural, relictual community tied specifically to areno-pedregosos soils, fitting securely within the Inhanduvá District and Espinhal Province, just like the local parks of *Prosopis affinis* (Inhanduvá). This linkage confirms its importance as a crucial component of the region's native woody flora.

However, the study issues a strong warning regarding the palm grove’s survival. Due to the chronic failure of natural recruitment resulting from cattle grazing, the community is failing to replace older individuals. The authors definitively state that the vegetation is **"muito frágil e susceptível à extinção, se mantidas as atuais condições de uso na área"** (very fragile and susceptible to extinction, if the current land use conditions are maintained). Therefore, immediate changes in land management are necessary to ensure the conservation and resilience of this unique habitat.

Key Quotes

  • "Descrito apenas em 1995, o palmar de Coatepe é presentemente analisado sob o ponto de vista fitogeográfico e inserido no Distrito do Inhanduvá e Província do Espinhal, segundo a classificação de Cabrera & Willink."

O INHANDUVÁ (PROSOPIS AFFINIS SPRENG) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL. 8 - ASPECTOS FITOGEOGRÁFICOS

JOSÉ NEWTON CARDOSO MARmORF; FABIANO DA SILVA ALVES (2011)

Abstract

São analisadas a distribuição de Prosopis affinis no Rio Grande do Sul, suas rotas imigratórias e a abrangência da Província do Espinhal no Estado.

Main Points

The study aims to analyze the distribution and migratory routes of *Prosopis affinis* (inhanduvá) and the geographic extent of the Espinhal Province in Rio Grande do Sul (RS). The authors confirm a much broader natural distribution of *P. affinis* than previously acknowledged, identifying relictual parks in various municipalities (Quaraí, São Vicente do Sul, Cacequi, Rosário do Sul, Alegrete) that contradict earlier literature limiting the species to a small area near Barra do Quaraí.

Phytogeographically, the Espinhal Province is represented by the Distrito do Inhanduvá in Western RS. This district is characterized by specific communities, including the *Nandubaysal*, defined by the co-occurrence of *P. affinis* and *Vachellia caven* (espinilho). The distribution of *P. affinis* is strongly linked to narrow sedimentary formations and alluvial deposits. The broad valley of the Ibicuí River is identified as the crucial migratory corridor that allowed the species to cross the basaltic Campanha Plateau, explaining the isolated occurrence of parks further east, interpreted as relictual fragments of a wider distribution during the late Pleistocene.

Ecologically, *P. affinis* is highly heliophilic. The expansion of taller riparian forest species (mata ciliar) during the Holocene's warmer, wetter climate led to increased shading, which compromised *P. affinis*'s permanence and caused the natural disappearance of many parks. This process of fragmentation was dramatically accelerated by human activity, particularly the introduction and expansion of rice cultivation (lavoura arrozeira), which led to the systematic destruction of these natural parks along the floodplains.

Conclusions

The study establishes that the natural occurrence of *Prosopis affinis* in Rio Grande do Sul is far more extensive than cited in limiting literature, with isolated parks representing crucial relictual fragments of the Espinhal Province. The species' distribution is primarily dictated by its strict edaphic requirement for sedimentary formations, explaining the migratory route along the Ibicuí River valley.

The authors specifically refute claims that the distribution of *P. affinis* is restricted by a single soil type (Gleissolo Melânico) or geographically confined, noting the species' wide distribution across South America in varied soils. They also reject the historical hypothesis of human introduction by Jesuits, arguing that the species lacked sufficient cultural importance to warrant cultivation, implying its presence is natural.

Regarding the thesis subject, *Vachellia caven* (espinilho) is confirmed as a co-occurring species in the *Nandubaysal* association. However, the authors conclude that *V. caven* is an extremely widespread native species in RS, inhabiting diverse terrains, including shallow soils derived from volcanic basalt on the Campanha Plateau. Its broad natural presence extends far beyond the specialized edaphic boundaries of the Espinhal Province (Distrito do Inhanduvá), meaning that its solitary presence is insufficient to define the phytogeographic unit, thus supporting its status as a fundamental, widely distributed native component of the region.

Key Quotes

  • "A presença natural do espinilho, por conseguinte, não basta para o reconhecimento de uma vegetação como integrante da Província do Espinhal ou, mais particularmente, de seu Distrito do Inhanduvá."
  • "O caso mais notável é o do espinilho (Vachellia caven), espécie de ampla distribuição nas áreas campestres do Rio Grande do Sul e que habita, inclusive, em solos rasos do Planalto da Campanha, gerados a partir de rochas vulcânicas (basalto)."
  • "Vale salientar que a distribuição desta espécie, além do Espinal, se estende pelas províncias fitogeográficas do 'Chaco, Monte e Paranaense', do centro da Argentina até o Paraguai e Bolívia, bem como a oeste dos Andes, entre Coquimbo e Concepción, no Chile."
  • "É no trecho sul desta planície, na região do 'Pontal do Quaraí', que se encontram os parques de inhanduvá mais biodiversos do Estado, em duas associações distintas: o parque de inhanduvá propriamente dito (Nandubaysal), marcado pela associação de Prosopis affinis (inhanduvá) e Vachellia caven (espinilho)."
  • "Deste modo, os parques de inhanduvá do Itapororó, de Cacequi, do Loreto e de Rosário do Sul podem ser interpretados como relictos do Distrito do Inhanduvá e Província do Espinhal no centro-oeste do Rio Grande do Sul."
  • "O derrame basáltico do Planalto da Campanha funcionou como barreira, limitando a expansão desta unidade fitogeográfica em extensas áreas no oeste do Rio Grande do Sul."
  • "A partir da introdução da lavoura arrozeira, a destruição dos parques naturais de inhanduvá foi acelerada por obra humana."
  • "A expansão das matas ciliares, favorecida no clima mais quente e úmido vivenciado no Holoceno, levou, certamente, ao desaparecimento de muitos parques de inhanduvá nas várzeas do rio Ibicuí e de seus afluentes."
  • "O inhanduvá favorece, inicialmente, a entrada de elementos oriundos da mata ciliar no interior do parque, os quais, por seu maior porte e consequente sombreamento, acabam por comprometer a permanência do Prosopis affinis na estrutura da vegetação."
  • "Não custa salientar, todavia, que não é mais possível aquilatar a verdadeira extensão destas unidades, mesmo num passado recente... uma vez que, em sua grande maioria, elas foram destruídas pela incúria humana (ou espírito imediatista)."

A paleontologia e suas aplicações: boletim de resumos

Dermeval A. do Carmo (organizador) (2003)

Abstract

Desde a Idade Antiga, os fósseis têm servido para instigar o pensamento científico a respeito da natureza. Em geral, atribuía-se aos fósseis uma origem sobrenatural, porém alguns gregos já lhes interpretavam como sendo relacionados a restos de organismos. Atualmente, o termo “fóssil” abrange todos restos e vestígios de organismos preservados nos sistemas naturais, seja em rochas, sedimentos, gelo ou âmbar. Esta compreensão moderna é mais eficaz, pois traduz a consolidação dos fundamentos da paleontologia e das ciências naturais no século XX. Porém, hoje em dia os desafios são maiores, pois a sociedade tem cobrado a aplicabilidade da pesquisa científica para o desenvolvimento humano e da própria sociedade. O Congresso Brasileiro de Paleontologia é um evento reconhecido em âmbito nacional e conquistou tradição nesta área do conhecimento. Em sua décima oitava edição, pela primeira vez na região centro-oeste, tem como objetivo registrar um marco na história da paleontologia brasileira com a participação de especialistas de renome internacional apresentando propostas técnico-científicas voltadas para áreas educacionais, empresariais e governamentais. Com este enfoque serão abordados diversos aspectos da Paleontologia, além de assuntos relacionados à geologia do petróleo, geologia ambiental, museologia e preservação do patrimônio geológico e paleontológico do Brasil. Além das sessões técnicas, os ciclos de conferências sobre PALEOECOLOGIA E PALEOAMBIENTE, BIOESTRATIGRAFIA APLICADA, PATRIMÔNIO FOSSILÍFERO, PALEOGEOGRAFIA DO NEÓGENO E QUATERNÁRIO e BIOTAS PRÉ-CAMBRIANAS, constituem um ponto de destaque deste evento. Serão também realizados simpósios em ENSINO DE CIÊNCIAS, EVOLUÇÃO BIOLÓGICA e, pela primeira vez neste congresso, o SIMPÓSIO DA AMPLA (Associação Latino-americana de Micropaleontologia). Para a realização deste evento, a UnB e a SBP receberam patrocínio de diversas instituições: Petróleo Brasileiro/SA – PETROBRAS, Patrocinador Máster, Coordenação de Aperfeiçoamento de Pessoal de Nível Superior – CAPES, Serviço Geológico do Brasil – CPRM, Universidade Católica de Goiás - UCG, Departamento Nacional da Produção Mineral – DNPM. Além destas instituições, contou-se com apoio da Associação Latino-americana de Micropaleontologia – AMPLA, e da Sociedade Brasileira de Geologia – SBG, em especial ao Núcleo de Brasília e à equipe de Computação Gráfica da UCG pela valiosa contribuição à programação visual do evento. Agradecemos também à Editora T. A. Queiroz, pela permissão de fotos do livro “Fósseis do Brasil”. Às instituições mencionadas e ao pessoal de todas as equipes, Comissão Organizadora, Comitê Científico, Comissão de Apoio, à administração da UnB, em especial ao Magnífico Reitor e ao Decanato de Assuntos Comunitários, aos diretores dos institutos de Geociências e de Ciências Biológicas, colegas, funcionários e alunos que diretamente participaram da organização do evento, apresento nossos agradecimentos. Em nome da Comissão Organizadora, venho dar as boas vindas à Brasília, esperando que a estada de todos seja enriquecedora e prazerosa. Brasília, 23 de maio de 2003 Prof. Dr. Dermeval Aparecido do Carmo Presidente da Comissão Organizadora XVIII Congresso Brasileiro de Paleontologia

Main Points

This document is the Boletim de Resumos (Abstract Bulletin) for the 18th Brazilian Congress of Paleontology, held in Brasília in July 2003. The organizing committee was chaired by Prof. Dr. Dermeval A. Do Carmo (IG/UnB).

The core scope of the congress was to highlight the modern relevance and 'applicability' of paleontological research, shifting focus from historical understanding toward practical contributions for human and societal development, targeting educational, entrepreneurial, and governmental sectors. Key thematic areas discussed included Paleontology, petroleum geology, environmental geology, museology, and the preservation of Brazilian geological and paleontological heritage.

Methods of dissemination included technical sessions and dedicated cycles of conferences focusing on highly specialized fields: Paleoecology and Paleoenvironment, Applied Biostratigraphy, Fossiliferous Heritage, Paleogeography of the Neogene and Quaternary, and Precambrian Biotas. Additionally, symposia were held on the Teaching of Sciences, Biological Evolution, and, for the first time, a symposium for AMPLA (Latin American Association of Micropaleontology).

Key supporting institutions and sponsors included PETROBRAS (Master Sponsor), CAPES, CPRM (Geological Service of Brazil), UCG, and DNPM (National Department of Mineral Production), demonstrating strong governmental and industry involvement.

Conclusions

The bulletin's 'Apresentação' concludes by stressing the historical significance of holding the 18th Congress in the Central-West region for the first time, aiming to mark a milestone in Brazilian paleontology by emphasizing applied research and interdisciplinary collaboration.

Emphasis is placed on the modern understanding of the term 'fossil' and the subsequent consolidation of Paleontology's foundation in the 20th century, which now drives the requirement for applicability to current societal challenges. The organizers express profound gratitude to all the individuals and institutions—including the administration of UnB, the organizing committees, and sponsors—whose collective effort made the extensive program possible. The bulletin serves as the formal record of this large-scale scientific gathering, concluding with well wishes for an 'enriching and pleasurable' stay for all attendees.

Misaligned Narrative of the Ecological Role of Vachellia caven in Eastern South American Savannas

N/A (N/A)

Abstract

Misaligned Narrative of the Ecological Role of Vachellia caven in Eastern South American Savannas Vachellia caven is a thorny leguminous shrub to treelet, widely distributed throughout the Neotropics and spanning across the Southern Cone from Bolivia, Paraguay and Brazil to Tierra del Fuego in Argentina and Chile. Most of the contemporary research focuses on the western range of the species distribution, in Chile, though this review emphasizes the species' long-term and widespread ecological importance in the eastern range, particularly within the Pampas of Southern South America. The Pampas is one of the most threatened open vegetation ecosystems, rapidly losing native habitats due to intense conversion for agriculture and livestock production. Driven by historical land use practices and the vast areas designated for livestock, xeric and spiny vegetation has long been suppressed and actively removed, as part of pasture management strategies. This review challenges the prevailing narrative that portrays V. caven as a controversial or ambiguous species, frequently labeled as "invasive woody encroacher". This designation, often documented in regions severely affected by conversion and overgrazing, reflects a socio-economic bias that emphasizes its purported negative impact on forage production while overlooking its ecological significance. The observed woody encroachment is fundamentally perceived as a symptom of anthropogenic degradation, including the historical removal of woody vegetation and chronic overgrazing. In contrast to this exploitative view, this xeric species acts as a crucial pioneer and "nurse" plant, essential for ecological succession and for sustaining a unique assemblage of native plants and animals. It facilitates the recruitment of other woody and herbaceous species by improving microhabitat conditions, including nitrogen enrichment and enhanced soil properties. By reframing V. caven’s encroachment as an indicator of ecosystem degradation rather than species invasiveness, we challenge the prevalent narrative that supports active removal of V. caven while underestimating its natural distributional range. Recognizing this species as fundamental to Pampas’ resilience and recovery is therefore essential for effective conservation and the development of sustainable restoration strategies.

Main Points

This review establishes a geographical critique, noting that current research heavily favors the western distribution of *Vachellia caven* (Chile), while the review focuses on the eastern range, specifically the threatened Pampas of Southern South America. The Pampas ecosystem is highlighted as suffering severe habitat loss due to agriculture and livestock conversion, where historical land use has actively suppressed and removed xeric vegetation like *V. caven* for pasture management.

The core of the analysis challenges the designation of *V. caven* as an "invasive woody encroacher." The authors argue that this label stems from a socio-economic bias focused primarily on maximizing forage production, thereby overlooking the species' substantial ecological role. Instead of being an invasive driver, the observed woody encroachment is reinterpreted as a direct consequence and symptom of anthropogenic degradation, specifically historical woody removal and chronic overgrazing.

The paper provides evidence of the species' positive ecological role, defining it as a crucial pioneer and "nurse" plant. This role involves improving microhabitat conditions—namely, through nitrogen enrichment and the enhancement of soil properties—which facilitates ecological succession and the successful recruitment of diverse native woody and herbaceous species.

Conclusions

The review concludes that the prevailing narrative supporting the active removal of *Vachellia caven* is flawed because it fails to account for the species' natural distribution and its fundamental ecological importance. By reframing the concept of encroachment from one of species invasiveness to one of ecosystem degradation, the authors reposition *V. caven* as an indicator of ecological stress rather than a causative agent.

Ultimately, the authors stress that recognizing *V. caven* as integral to the resilience and recovery mechanisms of the Pampas is paramount. This shift in perspective is deemed essential not only for achieving effective conservation outcomes but also for developing appropriate and sustainable restoration strategies within this highly threatened open vegetation ecosystem.

Key Quotes

  • "Misaligned Narrative of the Ecological Role of Vachellia caven in Eastern South American Savannas"
  • "The Pampas is one of the most threatened open vegetation ecosystems, rapidly losing native habitats due to intense conversion for agriculture and livestock production."
  • "Driven by historical land use practices and the vast areas designated for livestock, xeric and spiny vegetation has long been suppressed and actively removed, as part of pasture management strategies."
  • "This review challenges the prevailing narrative that portrays V. caven as a controversial or ambiguous species, frequently labeled as "invasive woody encroacher"."

Manual Técnico da Vegetação Brasileira

Instituto Brasileiro de Geografia e Estatística - IBGE (2012)

Abstract

É com grande satisfação que o Instituto Brasileiro de Geografia e Estatística - IBGE, por meio da Diretoria de Geociências, traz a público a segunda edição revista e ampliada do Manual técnico da vegetação brasileira. Esta edição representa a fusão de duas publicações anteriores do IBGE – Classificação da vegetação brasileira, adaptada a um sistema universal (1991) e Manual técnico da vegetação brasileira (1992) – e incorpora informações novas, derivadas dos mais recentes avanços do conhecimento sobre a cobertura vegetal nativa do Brasil. Com esse conteúdo, tal edição vem ao encontro da preocupação do IBGE com a constante atualização e melhoria da qualidade da informação prestada ao público. Esta obra está dividida em quatro capítulos: sistema fitogeográfico, inventário das formações florestais e campestres, técnicas e manejo de coleções botânicas e procedimentos para mapeamento da vegetação em escala regional. Nesses capítulos, estão descritos os conceitos, as etapas e os procedimentos metodológicos utilizados pela equipe de estudos de vegetação do IBGE para análise, caracterização, classificação e mapeamento da vegetação brasileira. Os capítulos e tópicos foram organizados de forma a permitir que os usuários, tanto no gabinete como no campo, tenham uma visão de conjunto do trabalho com vegetação realizado no IBGE. O conhecimento desses tópicos é considerado essencial para aqueles que estudam, pesquisam ou mapeiam as fisionomias vegetais do Brasil nos diversos níveis de levantamento, desde o regional até o de semidetalhe. Este Manual tem ainda como objetivo contribuir para a uniformização dos critérios e da terminologia adotados no Sistema de Classificação da Vegetação Brasileira.

Main Points

The IBGE's Technical Manual of Brazilian Vegetation is the second revised and expanded edition, merging two previous foundational publications (1991 and 1992) and incorporating up-to-date scientific knowledge regarding Brazil's native vegetation cover. Its overarching goal is to standardize the concepts, terminology, and methodologies used for the analysis, characterization, classification, and mapping of Brazilian vegetation by the IBGE team, ensuring high-quality and consistent information dissemination.

This manual is organized into four major chapters detailing the methodological procedures:
1. **Phytogeographic System (Sistema fitogeográfico):** This section provides the theoretical foundation, reviewing universal and national classification systems and establishing the hierarchical scheme (e.g., Domínio, Formação, Sinúsia). It introduces the official classification legend, which is crucial for defining ecosystems relevant to the thesis, such as *Estepe (Campos do sul do Brasil)*, which corresponds to the Pampas, and its sub-types (*Estepe Arborizada, Estepe Parque, Estepe Gramíneo-Lenhosa*). It also defines specialized categories like the *Sistema da Vegetação Secundária (Tratos Antrópicos)*, recognizing areas subject to human impact such as *Pecuária* (livestock).

2. **Inventory of Forest and Grassland Formations (Inventário das formações florestais e campestres):** This chapter focuses on practical methods for field assessment, covering different inventory types (reconnaissance, semi-detailed), various sampling techniques (systematic, stratified), and crucial procedures for quantifying the potential of woody/arboreal resources (*potencial lenhoso/arbóreo*) specifically within non-forest formations like Savana (Cerrado) and Savana-Estépica (Caatinga). This detailed focus on quantifying woody elements in grasslands is essential context for understanding the 'woody encroachment' phenomenon.

3. **Techniques and Management of Botanical Collections (Técnicas e manejo de coleções botânicas):** This section outlines standardized procedures for field collection, preservation (herborization, pressing, drying), labeling, and identification of botanical samples, ensuring the proper acquisition and maintenance of data required for species-level confirmation.

4. **Procedures for Regional Vegetation Mapping (Procedimentos para mapeamento da vegetação em escala regional):** This final chapter describes the technical workflow for cartographic production, spanning from literature review and base map preparation to digital image processing (georeferencing, enhancement), field validation, integration of data into databases, and final map generation (typically at scales from 1:250,000 to 1:1,000,000).

Conclusions

The primary conclusion of the manual, articulated in the presentation and introduction, is the imperative need for the uniform adoption of criteria and terminology within the Brazilian Vegetation Classification System. This standardization is deemed critical for researchers and mappers working at all levels of detail, from broad regional studies down to semi-detailed local surveys. The manual serves as the definitive reference to ensure methodological consistency across national studies of vegetation physiognomies.

The document explicitly validates and integrates the classification of human-altered areas into the system through the category *Sistema da Vegetação Secundária (Tratos Antrópicos)*, encompassing major land uses such as *Agricultura* and *Pecuária* (livestock). By officially including these anthropological treatments, the IBGE acknowledges the pervasive influence of human activities on the landscape structure, providing a framework against which ecological changes, such as woody proliferation, must be documented.

Furthermore, the manual stands as a continuation of established Brazilian phytogeography, paying homage to key figures like Henrique Pimenta Veloso, whose work laid the groundwork for the modern Brazilian Phytogeographic System in 1982. This continuity highlights the institutional commitment to rigorous, established scientific methods for monitoring and classifying the nation's diverse natural resources.

  • "Ministério do Planejamento, Orçamento e Gestão / Instituto Brasileiro de Geografia e Estatística - IBGE / Diretoria de Geociências / Coordenação de Recursos Naturais e Estudos Ambientais"
  • "Este Manual tem ainda como objetivo contribuir para a uniformização dos critérios e da terminologia adotados no Sistema de Classificação da Vegetação Brasileira."

Supports Soil and Biogeochemical CyclingPampas Ecosystem Degradation and ResilienceEcological Role and Nurse Effects

Ecuaciones alométricas para la estimación de biomasa total y componentes de Vachellia caven (Mol.) Seigler & Ebinger.

Di Paola, D. M. L.; Pazos Carrizo, D. V.; Felsinger, C. L.; Arturi, L. E.; Gristina, A. L.; Di Blasio, V. E.; Cisneros, M. V. (2016)

Abstract

Los modelos alométricos para la estimación de la biomasa son un indicador del carbono almacenado existente en los ecosistemas y se pueden estimar mediante modelos alométricos, que deben ser precisos, insesgados y locales. Los objetivos fueron cuantificar la biomasa individual de Vachellia caven y su distribución por componente estructural, estimar los factores de expansión de biomasa (FEB) por clase diamétrica, y obtener modelos alométricos para la estimación de la biomasa agregada en los arbustales nativos del Espinal (Entre Ríos). En 78 individuos de distintas clases diamétricas se midieron variables dasométricas y se determinó la biomasa área total y por componente (fuste, ramas mayores de 9 cm de diámetro, ramas menores de 9 cm, hojas y frutos) mediante el método destructivo. Para la selección de los mejores modelos de estimación se utilizaron indicadores de bondad de ajuste: coeficiente de determinación ajustado, error cuadrático medio de predicción, estadígrafo de Akaike (AIC) y el Índice de Furnival. Los modelos de mejor ajuste se basaron en el diámetro a la altura del pecho (DAP) y la altura total (EB=) y área de copa.

Main Points

The study focused on developing precise, localized allometric models for estimating both total and component biomass of *Vachellia caven* in the native scrublands of the Espinal (Entre Ríos, Argentina).

**Methods:** The researchers utilized a destructive sampling method on 78 individuals selected across distinct diameter classes. They measured key dendrometric variables. The biomass was meticulously divided and quantified for five specific structural components: stem (fuste), large branches (>9 cm in diameter), small branches (<9 cm in diameter), leaves, and fruits. To ensure model robustness and accuracy, various statistical indicators of goodness-of-fit were employed for model selection, including the Adjusted Coefficient of Determination ($R^2_{adj}$), Mean Square Error of Prediction (ECM), Akaike Information Criterion (AIC), and the Furnival Index.

**Results:** The resulting models demonstrated excellent fit and were deemed highly reliable. The most effective models utilized easily measurable field variables: Diameter at Breast Height (DBH/DAP), total height, and crown area. Crucially, the study successfully produced Biomass Expansion Factors (BFE) categorized by diameter class, which are essential for accurately scaling up individual biomass estimations to provide total aggregate biomass estimates across the Espinal’s native scrublands. This detailed component-based measurement provides fundamental data for understanding how carbon and nutrients are distributed within the plant structure.

Conclusions

The authors successfully established accurate and locally derived allometric models necessary for quantifying the biomass and associated carbon stocks of *Vachellia caven* in the native Espinal ecosystem. These precise estimations, which differentiate between structural components such as stems, branches, leaves, and fruits, are vital for detailed ecological studies, particularly those concerning nutrient cycling (e.g., nitrogen input via leaves and fruits) and the species' structural contribution to the habitat.

By providing reliable tools to quantify biomass non-destructively based on simple metrics (DBH, height, crown area), the research supports better ecological characterization and management. This foundational quantitative data affirms the species' significant structural role, implicitly supporting the thesis by providing the necessary input for assessing its ecological value and resilience function in the Eastern South American Savannas/Pampas region, contrasting the simplistic 'woody encroacher' label.

  • "cuantificar la biomasa individual de Vachellia caven y su distribución por componente estructural."
  • "obtener modelos alométricos para la estimación de la biomasa agregada en los arbustales nativos del Espinal (Entre Ríos)."
