Coalescent‐based species delimitation in North American pinyon pines using low‐copy nuclear genes and plastomes

José‐Rubén Montes, Pablo Peláez, Alejandra Moreno‐Letelier, David S. Gernandt (2022)

Abstract

Premise: Accurate species delimitation is essential for evolutionary biology, conservation, and biodiversity management. We studied species delimitation in North American pinyon pines, Pinus subsection Cembroides, a natural group with high levels of incomplete lineage sorting. Methods: We used coalescent‐based methods and multivariate analyses of low‐copy number nuclear genes and nearly complete high‐copy number plastomes generated with the Hyb‐Seq method. The three coalescent‐based species delimitation methods evaluated were the Generalized Mixed Yule Coalescent (GMYC), Poisson Tree Process (PTP), and Trinomial Distribution of Triplets (Tr2). We also measured admixture in populations with possible introgression. Results: Our results show inconsistencies among GMYC, PTP, and Tr2. The single‐ locus based GMYC analysis of plastid DNA recovered a higher number of species (up to 24 entities, including singleton lineages and clusters) than PTP and the multi‐ locus coalescent approach. The PTP analysis identiﬁed 10 species whereas Tr2 recovered 13, which agreed closely with taxonomic treatments. Conclusions: We found that PTP and GMYC identiﬁed species with low levels of ILS and high morphological divergence (P. maximartinezii, P. pinceana, and P. rzedowskii). However, GMYC method oversplit species by identiﬁcation of more divergent samples as singletons. Moreover, both PTP and GMYC were incapable of identifying some species that are readily identiﬁed morphologically. We suggest that the divergence times between lineages within North American pinyon pines are so disparate that GMYC results are unreliable. Results of the Tr2 method coincided well with previous delimitations based on morphology, DNA, geography, and secondary chemistry.

Main Points

### Methods

The study aimed to infer species boundaries in *Pinus subsection Cembroides* (North American pinyon pines), a group known for high levels of incomplete lineage sorting (ILS). The authors employed coalescent-based methods and used the Hyb-Seq sequencing approach to generate data from 207 low-copy nuclear genes and nearly complete plastomes. A total of 93 individuals were sampled, including 80 from the target subsection.

Three coalescent-based species delimitation methods were evaluated and compared: the single-locus Generalized Mixed Yule Coalescent (GMYC), the Poisson Tree Process (PTP), and the multi-locus Trinomial Distribution of Triplets (Tr2). Data processing included stringent filtering of nuclear genes to exclude paralogs and sequences with low pairwise identity or anomalously high substitution rates. Phylogenetic analysis utilized Maximum Likelihood (RAxML) and Bayesian inference (MrBayes) on both concatenated nuclear genes and partitioned plastome sequences.

### Results

The three methods provided inconsistent results regarding species counts. The single-locus GMYC analysis, particularly when applied to plastid DNA, severely oversplit the taxa, recovering up to 24 distinct entities. In comparison, the PTP analysis identified 10 species, while the multi-locus Tr2 analysis recovered 13 species.

The Tr2 results were found to agree closely with established taxonomic treatments. PTP and GMYC were successful in identifying species characterized by low ILS and high morphological divergence (*P. maximartinezii*, *P. pinceana*, and *P. rzedowskii*). However, the GMYC method tended to oversplit taxa by identifying divergent samples as singletons. Furthermore, both PTP and GMYC failed to identify several species that are readily distinguishable based solely on morphology.

Conclusions

The authors concluded that accurate species delimitation in *Pinus subsection Cembroides* is complicated by disparate divergence times among lineages and the widespread presence of incomplete lineage sorting (ILS). They suggested that this evolutionary complexity renders single-locus methods, such as GMYC, unreliable, noting that GMYC significantly oversplit species (up to 24 entities recovered). They explicitly stated that the divergence times were so disparate that GMYC results were untrustworthy.

The study highlighted the superior performance of the multi-locus coalescent approach, Tr2, whose results coincided well with previous taxonomic delimitations established through the integration of multiple data streams, including morphology, DNA, geography, and secondary chemistry. This finding advocates for using objective multi-locus methods that corroborate evidence from traditional taxonomic fields to achieve reliable species boundaries for conservation and management purposes.

Key Quotes

  • "Accurate species delimitation is essential for evolutionary biology, conservation, and biodiversity management."
  • "Species are fundamental units of study in several areas of the biological sciences."
  • "The accurate delimitation of species boundaries is essential for evolutionary biology, conserva- tion biology, and biodiversity management (Sites and Crandall, 1997; Sites and Marshall, 2003; Yang and Rannala, 2010)."
  • "Interest in integrative species delimitation has grown thanks to the increasing availability of molecular data, new approaches, and methods (Schlick‐Steiner et al., 2010; Fujita et al., 2012; Zhang et al., 2013) that have been developed to test species boundaries."
  • "Coalescent‐based methods provide an attractive alternative for studying the evolutionary processes that contribute to speciation, inferring the relationships among species, and delimiting independent evolutionary lineages objectively in the presence of gene‐tree conﬂict (Fujita et al., 2012; Smith et al., 2015, 2020; Luo et al., 2018)."
  • "In pines and other conifers, there are few studies using objective methods for the delimitation of species."
  • "Lineage delimitation of trees is also diﬃcult because of complex evolutionary histories caused by incomplete lineage sorting (ILS) and reticulation resulting from hybridization and introgression (Rosenberg, 2003; Hernández‐León et al., 2013; Zhang et al., 2014)."
  • "The International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN, 2019) lists ﬁve pinyon pine taxa as vulnerable or endangered whereas the Mexican government lists nine as protected (SEMARNAT, 2010)."
  • "The circumscription of recognized species in Pinus subsect. Cembroides diﬀers in recent works (Gernandt et al., 2005; Farjon and Filer, 2013; Gernandt and Pérez de la Rosa, 2014; Montes et al., 2019) and the taxonomic ranges used for pinyon pines has varied widely..."
  • "Results of the Tr2 method coincided well with previous delimitations based on morphology, DNA, geography, and secondary chemistry."

Restauración de Ecosistemas Forestales [Título Deduced]

Jan R. Bannister, Juan F. Ovalle, Rodrigo Vargas-Gaete, Vivianne Claramunt-Torche (Editores) (2024)

Abstract

Un nublado y frío martes 9 de julio del 2019 en Concepción, luego de una reunión del directorio de la Red Chilena de Restauración Ecológica, fuimos a un bar en el barrio Universitario de la ciudad para conversar y discutir sobre el futuro de la restauración en Chile. Tras algunas cervezas y sabrosas anécdotas, emergió una interesante discusión respecto a lo desagregada que se encontraba la información e investigación sobre restauración, así como la brecha que existía para que estudiantes, técnicos y profesionales interesados en restaurar, pudieran acceder a conocimientos teóricos y prácticos actualizados y en español. Gran parte del conocimiento se encontraba disperso en cientos de artículos en inglés, en revistas de acceso restringido o en libros difíciles de conseguir, y donde abundan los ejemplos de restauración propios de ecosistemas del hemisferio norte. Sin saber muy bien en lo que se iba a convertir este proyecto, nos preguntamos de forma muy ingenua: ¿Y si escribimos un libro de restauración de ecosistemas forestales para un público hispanohablante? La idea en simple era sintetizar el conocimiento existente, sistematizar en un solo libro la diversidad de tópicos que tratan de forma separada los libros de restauración, y no contentos con eso, presentar el contenido teórico-práctico de forma atractiva y lúdica para un estudiante, intentando innovar frente al tradicional formato de literatura técnica disponible en librerías chilenas. Quedamos muy entusiasmados/as con la idea, y pocas semanas después comenzó el trabajo, el cual ilusamente pensamos que tomaría, como mucho, dos años, ¡pero fueron 5 años!

Main Points

This text provides the table of contents and introductory material (Preface and Prologues) for a comprehensive book dedicated to forest ecosystem restoration, primarily focusing on Chile and Southern South America.

The text outlines the ambitious scope and structure of the book, which synthesizes dispersed knowledge, systematizing it into five main sections:

1. **Introduction (Part I):** Covers the history of degradation and restoration efforts in Chile, establishing the need for the book.
2. **Theoretical Foundations (Part II):** Addresses key ecological and managerial concepts crucial for restoration, including landscape ecology, genetics, ecophysiology, silviculture (a key tool for restoring degraded forests), and the recovery of biodiversity and ecosystem services.
3. **Social and Economic Dimension (Part III):** Focuses on the human element, discussing social inclusion, professional training, governance, policy, and the socio-economic valuation of restoration.
4. **Elements of a Restoration Project (Part IV):** Detailed methodology, including natural regeneration strategies, native seed supply chains, nursery production, specific revegetation techniques (Chapter 17, highly detailed), statistical evaluation, and incorporating local actors’ knowledge.
5. **Practical Experiences (Part V):** Case studies covering specific disturbances and environments, such as post-fire recovery, mine rehabilitation, converting exotic plantations back to native forest, managing exotic invasive species (Chapter 23), and restoration in agricultural and urban landscapes.

The project was driven by the recognition of a significant knowledge gap, where updated, practical, and Spanish-language resources specifically tailored to Southern South American ecosystems were lacking. The creation of the book involved a massive collaborative effort over five years, engaging four editors, 25 authors, 74 co-authors, and 34 external reviewers.

Conclusions

The editors and contributors conclude that the book successfully achieved its goal of synthesizing and systematizing the theoretical and practical knowledge surrounding forest restoration in Southern South America. This collaborative work aims to serve as a foundational ‘cabecera’ (cornerstone) text for students and professionals across Hispanoamérica, filling the critical void left by fragmented, often English-language literature focusing mainly on Northern Hemisphere ecosystems.

Two key conclusions arise from the prologues:

First, the effort is timely, aligning with major national policy objectives, such as Chile's **Plan Nacional de Restauración de Paisajes**, which seeks to restore 1 million hectares by 2030. The book provides essential conceptual bases and technical guidelines to realize these large-scale goals, recognizing that restoration is a difficult process often 'full of errors' but necessary for reversing degradation.

Second, the comprehensive nature of the volume—covering natural sciences, engineering, economics, and social sciences—provides a detailed manual relevant globally, helping to advance the necessary shift toward a 'cultura de restauración,' ensuring that theory and practice are diffused widely from the 'last corner of South America.'

RECONSTITUIÇÃO PALEOAMBIENTAL EM REMANESCENTE DE SAVANA ESTÉPICA PARQUE NO EXTREMO OESTE DO RIO GRANDE DO SUL (BARRA DO QUARAÍ), COM BASE EM PALINOMORFOS HOLOCÊNICOS

Andreia Cardoso Pacheco Evaldt (2013)

Abstract

A Savana Estépica Parque, formação vegetacional campestre do Bioma Pampa, tem sua área de ocorrência no Brasil restrita ao extremo oeste do Rio Grande do Sul, no município de Barra do Quaraí. Com o objetivo estudar a história vegetacional desta formação e suas mudanças ao longo do Holoceno tardio, foi desenvolvida a pesquisa em um afloramento localizado na margem brasileira do rio Quaraí (30°16’27.9”S e 57°26’33.6”O), com a coleta de 86 amostras. Para determinação do espectro polínico atual, foram coletadas 15 amostras superficiais em diferentes ambientes do Parque do Espinilho (PESP). Um total de 81 táxons foi identificado nas amostras sedimentares do afloramento (10 férteis) e 114 nas amostras superficiais. Análises a partir dos diagramas polínicos foram realizadas apoiadas por datações radiocarbônicas e análises granulométricas. Os resultados indicam que entre 3.380 ± 25 e 2.350 ± 25 anos AP a área era composta por uma planície de inundação recoberta por gramíneas que formava corpos d’água de pequena profundidade, possibilitando o desenvolvimento de colônias de algas. Entre 2.328 e 2.262 anos AP observa-se diminuição da umidade e aumento de temperatura, evidenciado pelo desaparecimento das algas e maior frequência de briófitos. Entre 2.130 e 1.940 ± 20 anos AP é registrado aumento de umidade refletido na maior diversidade de táxons arbóreos, com expansão da Mata Ciliar. Os dados de granulometria corroboram com os dados palinológicos. O espectro polínico das amostras superficiais refletiu a composição taxonômica da flora do PESP, de acordo com a particularidade ecológica de cada ponto de amostragem. Este constitui o primeiro trabalho de palinologia desenvolvido na Savana Estépica Parque nos três países em que ocorre (Argentina Uruguai e Brasil). Os resultados aqui apresentados contribuirão para melhor compreensão da origem e desenvolvimento desta formação vegetacional, importante pelo endemismo de suas espécies e que está sob forte pressão antrópica por ocorrer em planícies de inundação, área de interesse para atividades agrícolas.

Main Points

The study utilized palynological analysis of 86 sediment samples from an outcrop on the Quaraí River margin, supported by 15 modern surface samples, radiocarbon dating, and granulometry, to reconstruct the vegetation history of the Savana Estépica Parque (Pampa Biome) in Barra do Quaraí during the Late Holocene.

Results identified 81 taxa in the sediment profile and 114 in the surface samples. The paleoenvironmental reconstruction demonstrated distinct phases:

* **3,380 ± 25 to 2,350 ± 25 yr BP:** The environment was characterized as a flood plain dominated by grasses, featuring shallow water bodies suitable for the proliferation of algal colonies, indicating high moisture.
* **2,328 to 2,262 yr BP:** A climatic shift occurred, marked by a noticeable decrease in humidity and an increase in temperature. This was evidenced by the disappearance of algae and a rise in the frequency of bryophytes.
* **2,130 to 1,940 ± 20 yr BP:** A final phase of increased humidity was recorded, leading to greater diversity among arboreal taxa and the consequent expansion of the *Mata Ciliar* (Gallery Forest). The accompanying granulometric data consistently corroborated these palynological interpretations of environmental changes.

Conclusions

This work is cited as the first palynological study developed within the Savana Estépica Parque across all three nations where it is present (Argentina, Uruguay, and Brazil), providing foundational data for conservation efforts.

The research successfully mapped the dynamic shifts of the Late Holocene environment, demonstrating natural oscillations between wet and slightly drier phases, which directly influenced the dominance of grasses versus arboreal species (such as the Gallery Forest).

Crucially, the study concludes by highlighting the contemporary vulnerability of this ecosystem. The formation is recognized for the endemism of its species but faces **strong anthropogenic pressure** because it naturally occurs in flood plains, making these areas highly desirable and subject to conversion for agricultural activities. The detailed historical context provided by the paleoenvironmental reconstruction is therefore essential for developing effective conservation and management strategies for this unique and threatened Pampa habitat.

Key Quotes

  • "A Savana Estépica Parque, formação vegetacional campestre do Bioma Pampa, tem sua área de ocorrência no Brasil restrita ao extremo oeste do Rio Grande do Sul, no município de Barra do Quaraí."
  • "Este constitui o primeiro trabalho de palinologia desenvolvido na Savana Estépica Parque nos três países em que ocorre (Argentina Uruguai e Brasil)."
  • "Os resultados aqui apresentados contribuirão para melhor compreensão da origem e desenvolvimento desta formação vegetacional, importante pelo endemismo de suas espécies..."
  • "...e que está sob forte pressão antrópica por ocorrer em planícies de inundação, área de interesse para atividades agrícolas."
  • "O conhecimento da palinologia do Quaternário na Campanha oeste do Rio Grande do Sul (RS), quando comparado às demais regiões fitofisiográficas do Estado, mostra-se extremamente defasado, com raros e espaçados esforços."
  • "Entre 2.130 e 1.940 ± 20 anos AP é registrado aumento de umidade refletido na maior diversidade de táxons arbóreos, com expansão da Mata Ciliar."
  • "Entre 3.380 ± 25 e 2.350 ± 25 anos AP a área era composta por uma planície de inundação recoberta por gramíneas..."
  • "Vachellia caven (Mol.) Seigler & Ebinger."
  • "Inferências paleoambientais e paleoclimáticas são realizadas através da análise dos registros palinológicos."
  • "Os dados de granulometria corroboram com os dados palinológicos."

PAUTAS PARA EL MANEJO DEL CAMPO NATURAL

Marcos Martínez, Marcelo Pereira (2011)

Abstract

Abstract not provided. This document is a technical manual starting with a table of contents (SUMARIO).

Main Points

This technical guide focuses on the management of natural grasslands (pastizal natural) for livestock production, primarily in the context of the Uruguayan Pampas. The text first classifies grass species (Poaceas) based on their cycle (Perennial/Annual, Estival/Invernal) and habit (Estoloníferas, Rizomatosas, Cespitosas), emphasizing the agronomic relevance of classifying them as Fine, Tender, Ordinary, or Hard grasses.

Non-grass species are categorized, notably including "Malezas de campo sucio" (weeds of dirty field) such as Chircas, Carquejas, and Mío Mío—species described as having woody or spiny structures and low palatability except when young. Legumes are noted as being very scarce in these natural fields.

The core of the guide centers on three main management variables, ranked by importance: animal stocking rate (Carga o dotación animal), sheep/cattle ratio (Relación ovino/bovino), and grazing system (Sistema de pastoreo). Determining the appropriate "Capacidad de carga" (carrying capacity, detailed in a table by soil type, e.g., 0.50–0.55 UG/ha for Basalto superficial rojo) is presented as the most crucial management decision. The text explicitly defines overgrazing (sobrecarga) as maintaining animal numbers above carrying capacity, which breaks the equilibrium and degrades the pasture, irrespective of the grazing system used.

The guide outlines the severe symptoms of degradation resulting from chronic overgrazing: species reduction (loss of fine perennial winter grasses), a shift towards estival cycles, increased bare soil (promoting erosion and evaporation), and proliferation of aggressive annual grasses and malezas, such as Gramilla Brava (Cynodon dactylon). If degradation is severe, the ultimate management necessity is to completely destroy the natural field using total herbicides or tilling and transitioning to cultivated crops/green feed.

Conclusions

The primary conclusion is that achieving "producción sustentable" (sustainable production) in natural grasslands depends fundamentally on maintaining a stocking rate (carga) adjusted to the field's specific carrying capacity. Errors in determining the load cannot be compensated for by adjustments to grazing systems.

Overloading initiates a clear pathway of degradation, resulting in the loss of desirable perennial grass species and the subsequent ecological replacement by less productive annual grasses and weeds. The objective of management is to maintain the highest possible percentage of productive grass cover and high utilization rates, which often means suppressing species classified as 'malezas de campo sucio.'

While differential grazing systems (pastoreo diferido) can slightly increase forage production (10–20%) and manage composition by promoting erect grasses (cespitosas), they are not a viable solution for chronic overgrazing. High sheep/cattle ratios are discouraged as they tend to promote less manageable estival, erect species. The overall final conclusion emphasizes minimizing soil exposure and avoiding degradation to prevent the catastrophic necessity of eliminating the natural pasture entirely through aggressive means (herbicides and rotation). The entire framework reinforces a production-centric view where woody or spiny species are defined as undesirable obstacles ('malezas').

Key Quotes

  • "El campo natural, o mejor denominado pastizal natural, está compuesto por muchas especies, lo que le confiere una diferencia fundamental con respecto a las pasturas cultivadas (praderas y verdeos)."
  • "La familia más numerosa en nuestros pastizales naturales y que a su vez, reúne las especies de mayor valor productivo para la ganadería, es la de las gramíneas."
  • "Pastos ordinarios: tienen baja apetecibilidad, limitada generalmente al estado más o menos juvenil. Su productividad es de media a baja, y son mejor aprovechadas con altas dotaciones de animales, lo que no permite acumular hojas viejas."
  • "Malezas de campo sucio: Son aquellas especies que por su porte, sobresalen del tapiz, presentando estructura más leñosas, como tallos, en el caso de las Chircas, Carquejas o Mío Mío, o espinosas como la Cardilla o el Caraguatá."
  • "Este tipo de malezas no son apetecidas por el ganado, o lo son cuando son plantas jóvenes."
  • "La variable de manejo más importante es la carga. Si nos equivocamos al determinarla, este error no podrá ser corregido realizando otro tipo de manejo, por ejemplo modificando el sistema de pastoreo."
  • "Capacidad de carga: Definimos capacidad de carga, como la dotación que puede soportar un campo, teniendo en cuenta un determinado objetivo de comportamiento productivo y de manejo, sin que el recurso campo natural se deteriore."
  • "Cuando se mantiene un número de animales mayor a la capacidad de carga de la comunidad vegetal, se determina una sobrecarga, y se rompe el equilibrio entre la composición de especies y la producción animal, degradando la pastura."
  • "Esto da lugar a un mayor porcentaje de suelo desnudo, o sea, suelo sin cobertura vegetal que lo proteja de la erosión por lluvia."
  • "Cuando un campo es totalmente ocupado por esta especie [Gramilla Brava], se deberá roturar o quemar con herbicidas totales y luego, organizar un ciclo de cultivos y verdeos para eliminar la maleza, lo cual genera como resultado la pérdida total del campo natural."
Contradicts Ecological Role and Nurse EffectsConservation and Restoration StrategiesWoody Encroachment Dynamics

Far from dismantled: Reply to “dispersal syndromes of Vachellia caven” by Velasco et al., 2023

Meredith Root-Bernstein, Matías Guerrero-Gatica, Natalia A. Villavicencio (2024)

Abstract

Sir, Velasco et al. (2023) conclude that the only reasonable explanation for the presence of Vachellia [Acacia] caven in Chile (west of the Andes) is human transport during the Holocene, making it an invasive archeophyte. They present a poorly argued review which would have benefited from a better empirical grounding. A systematic review, rather than a traditional review, might have helped to get a broader overview of the literature. At the same time, the way in which the evidence was evaluated is also problematic. We believe that the question of Vachellia [Acacia] caven’s origins remains entirely unresolved.

Main Points

This correspondence critically analyzes and refutes the arguments made by Velasco et al. (2023) classifying *Vachellia caven* in Chile as an invasive archeophyte, asserting that the question of its origin remains unresolved.

First, the authors challenge the evidentiary basis. They argue that the lack of fossil pollen evidence for *V. caven* west of the Andes is meaningless, as pollen fossilization is rare and evidence is similarly lacking east of the Andes. They also critique the precision of speciation estimates used to rule out natural dispersal before the Andes reached their maximum height.

Second, the core of the critique focuses on dispersal mechanisms. The authors argue that applying criteria of 'probability' or 'parsimony' to long-distance dispersal (LDD) is irrelevant, as LDD is inherently improbable and often trait-neutral over long time periods, yet numerous species have crossed the Andes. They dismiss the requirement that a disperser must cover 165 km in a single digestive event as an 'irrelevant and inaccurate criterion.' Instead, they propose a plausible low-frequency, non-human mechanism: endozoochory by large herbivores (like guanacos or extinct megafauna) through Andean passes, followed by hydrochory (washout) via rivers into central Chile.

Third, the paper reinforces the historical and ecological context. Extinct megafauna (e.g., Notiomastodon, giant ground sloths, extinct camelids) had high-Andean distributions and could have served as trans-Andean dispersers during the Pleistocene. Furthermore, they highlight that *V. caven* is a crucial pioneer species establishing post-disturbance, facilitated by livestock endozoochory, which acts as a proxy for megafauna. Crucially, they emphasize that *V. caven* 'dominates an early-succession formation and facilitates forest trees which later overshade it,' directly contradicting any purely negative view of its establishment.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the fundamental premise of the Velasco et al. paper—that LDD must be a 'highly likely' event—is a misunderstanding, rendering their arguments based on low probability irrelevant. They assert that dismissing non-human dispersal mechanisms demonstrates a lack of knowledge and imagination regarding the species and the mechanisms involved.

Ultimately, they argue that **all scenarios for the origin of *Vachellia caven* remain plausible**, including natural vicariance or trans-Andean spread, potentially involving multiple dispersal events and mechanisms (including human transport). There is insufficient evidence to justify recategorizing the species as an invasive archeophyte.

Finally, the authors issue a strong conservation warning: recategorization as invasive poses a significant risk of 'exposing the species to lowered conservation protections.' They state that arguments allowing land conversion based on an 'invasive' label would be welcomed by developers and would undermine the natural successional process toward native forest that *V. caven* facilitates.

Key Quotes

  • "We believe that the question of Vachellia [Acacia] caven’s origins remains entirely unresolved."
  • "Lack of evidence for something is not evidence for anything."
  • "To the contrary, long-distance dispersal is inherently improbable."
  • "It is thus irrelevant to make arguments about the probability of dispersal events when discussing long-distance dispersal across the Andes."
  • "We also believe that there are plausible, if inherently low-probability or low-frequency non-human dispersal mechanisms by which V. caven could have crossed the Andes."
  • "We argue that a seed could potentially travel half-way over the Andes by endozoochory and then be washed the rest of the way in a flood event or along a river."
  • "V. caven is a pioneer species establishing in open patches post disturbance. It dominates an early-succession formation and facilitates forest trees which later overshade it."
  • "Cattle may of course act as proxies for extinct megafauna, as the authors acknowledge, but discarding the possibility of megafauna as dispersers because megafaunal dispersal events could only have occurred in the late Pleistocene or early Holocene—when the megafauna were already in decline and would have thus supposedly resulted in a patchy V. caven distribution—is premature, for all the same reasons stated above."
  • "Fundamentally, the authors misunderstand that long-distance dispersal is not a highly likely event but rather a trait-neutral fundamentally improbable event. All of their arguments about low probabilities are thus irrelevant."
  • "All scenarios for the origin of Vachellia [Acacia] caven remain plausible and there is no evidence justifying recategorising the species as an invasive archeophyte. Such a recategorization risks exposing the species to lowered conservation protections."

Primer Inventario Nacional de Bosques Nativos. INFORME REGIONAL ESPINAL

República Argentina. Secretaría de Ambiente y Desarrollo Sustentable (SAyDS), Dirección de Bosques, Proyecto Bosques Nativos y Áreas Protegidas BIRF 4085-AR (2007)

Abstract

Al iniciar el inventario, la superficie de bosque nativo de la Argentina se estimaba en aproximadamente 40 millones de hectáreas. Sin embargo nunca se había realizado un inventario total de bosques nativos, lo cual significa que existe una escasez de información confiable sobre la magnitud, distribución y condiciones de estos bosques. Por la misma razón, no se ha podido ordenar el uso sustentable de los mismos, evaluar las amenazas ambientales y crear una base de datos sobre la cual basar un análisis de las opciones políticas. El convenio de Préstamo Nº 4085-AR suscrito entre el Estado Argentino y el BIRF (Banco Internacional de Reconstrucción y Fomento) pretende resolver esta falta a través del Primer Inventario Nacional de Bosques Nativos y del Establecimiento de un Banco de Datos. Los principales objetivos del Proyecto son: • Obtener información básica sobre los recursos forestales nativos; • Crear y mantener una base de datos actualizada de dichos recursos; y • Reforzar la capacidad operativa de la Secretaría de Ambiente y Desarrollo Sustentable (SAyDS) para el manejo y uso de la base de datos. Esta información suministrará la base imprescindible para reformar el marco político, legal y regulador que afecta a los bosques nativos, para iniciar la investigación aplicada y los estudios complementarios para lograr la ordenación forestal, el uso racional y la conservación de los bosques nativos.

Main Points

The *Primer Inventario Nacional de Bosques Nativos* (First National Inventory of Native Forests) was conducted under the BIRF 4085-AR project to address a critical scarcity of reliable data regarding the magnitude, distribution, and condition of Argentina’s native forests, previously estimated around 40 million hectares. This lack of information hampered sustainable use planning and policy development.

### Methodology
The inventory spanned six phytogeographical regions, with this specific report focusing on the **Espinal** region. The work was contracted to a consortium, eventually led by Aeroterra S.A.

Crucially, the methodology used for the Espinal region, as well as the Monte region, was limited to an *inventario de superficies* (surface inventory), meaning **no terrestrial measurements** of the forest mass were performed. Data acquisition relied entirely on interpreting LANDSAT TM satellite images (1997-2000), supported by cartography and GIS (SIG).

Georeferencing utilized ERDAS IMAGINE software and 1:250,000 scale topographic and image maps from the Instituto Geográfico Militar (IGM). Forest stratification was achieved through visual interpretation of printed images (TM bands 3, 4, and 5) and controls via aerial flights.

### Results (Espinal Region)
The Espinal region covers a total area of 329,395 km². Out of this, **Forest Lands (Tierras Forestales) occupy 7.5%**, totaling 24,881 km².

These limited forest areas are predominantly concentrated in the Caldén District. The main formation identified is the **Caldenales** (forests of *Prosopis caldenia*), characterized as xerophilous and relatively open woodland structures, typically reaching eight to ten meters in height.

Conclusions

The core conclusion articulated in the Prologue by Secretary Dra. Romina Picolotti emphasizes the successful establishment of a quantifiable baseline for the National Native Forest Patrimony and the creation of the UMSEF (Unit for Management of the Forest Evaluation System).

This objective data base is intended to strengthen the National Forest Plan and will be mandated under a new State Policy that prioritizes environmental quality and the rights of the populations inhabiting these forests. The overarching policy goal is to create a robust legal instrument to establish minimum protection budgets for native forests.

Ultimately, the inventory is the foundational tool required to control and reverse the ongoing process of **“desmonte indiscriminado”** (indiscriminate clearing). The authors starkly conclude that this deforestation has resulted in the loss of approximately 70% of Argentina’s original native forest mass over the last century. Stopping this process is deemed essential to protect local communities, conserve biodiversity, and ensure the long-term sustainability of Argentina’s native forest resources.

Key Quotes

  • "se logró cuantificar por primera vez el Patrimonio Forestal Nativo de nuestro país"
  • "se podrá controlar y revertir el desmonte indiscriminado que ha reducido en cien años cerca del 70 % de la superficie originaria de nuestra masa forestal autóctona."
  • "para frenar este proceso que afecta a la gente, a la biodiversidad y a la sustentabilidad del bosque nativo argentino"
  • "Obtener información básica sobre los recursos forestales nativos;"
  • "Esta información suministrará la base imprescindible para reformar el marco político, legal y regulador que afecta a los bosques nativos, para iniciar la investigación aplicada y los estudios complementarios para lograr la ordenación forestal, el uso racional y la conservación de los bosques nativos."
  • "Aunque la metodología seguida para el tratamiento de cada una de las regiones es muy similar, el presente informe regional sólo trata de la región Espinal."
  • "De acuerdo con los términos del contrato, en esta región y en la región del Monte, no se han realizado mediciones terrestres con el fin de inventariar la masa forestal."

EFEITOS DO PASTOREIO SOBRE A VEGETAÇÃO NATURAL EM FRAGMENTO DE SAVANA ESTÉPICA PARQUE, RIO GRANDE DO SUL, BRASIL

Cristina Gouvêa Redin (2013)

Abstract

Dissertação de Mestrado Programa de Pós-Graduação em Engenharia Florestal Universidade Federal de Santa Maria EFEITOS DO PASTOREIO SOBRE A VEGETAÇÃO NATURAL EM FRAGMENTO DE SAVANA ESTÉPICA PARQUE, RIO GRANDE DO SUL, BRASIL AUTORA: CRISTINA GOUVÊA REDIN ORIENTADOR: SOLON JONAS LONGHI Data e Local da Defesa: Santa Maria, 27 de fevereiro de 2013. Apesar de ocupar lugar de destaque na flora sulina, a região pertencente ao Parque Estadual do Espinilho, inserido dentro dos domínios fitogeográficos da Savana Estépica Parque, ainda é pouco investigada pela ciência. Características da vegetação, tais como denso estrato herbáceo e a presença de árvores isoladas, configuram-na como propícia à atividade pecuarista. Valendo-se desse fato, o presente estudo objetivou analisar alterações florísticas e edáficas, impostas pelo pastoreio. Para tanto, foram selecionadas duas área de estudo, uma sob pastoreio e outra excluída dessa atividade a cinco anos, ambas contendo uma unidade amostral de 2 ha, subdividida em 200 subunidades amostrais de 100 m². Foi realizado inventário do estrato arbóreo e regenerante em 100 dessas subunidades amostrais e coleta de dados das demais variáveis em 50 subunidades. A dissertação foi dividida em dois capítulos com objetivos específicos de analisar a similaridade, alterações estruturais e florísticas na vegetação arbórea e regenerante (Capítulo I), avaliar alterações em propriedades físicas do solo e biomassa aérea total do estrato herbáceo entre as áreas, bem como investigar possíveis correlações entre essas variáveis e a abundância das principais espécies presentes na regeneração (Prosopis affinis Spreng. e Vachellia caven (Molina) Seigler & Ebinger) (Capítulo II). Por meio de estudos referentes a atributos fitossociológicos e estruturais, pode- se perceber notáveis diferenças entre as áreas, principalmente quanto à estrutura diamétrica da vegetação e composição florística da regeneração natural, sendo Vachellia caven a espécie melhor adaptada ao pastejo, ao contrário de Prosopis affinis. O resultado para similaridade entre as áreas, conforme expresso pelo índice de Jaccard, é de média similaridade (75%). Em relação às variáveis físicas do solo e biomassa aérea total do estrato herbáceo constataram-se diferenças significativas entre áreas, evidenciadas por meio de testes-T de Student. Os testes de correlação, realizados pelo método de Spearman, mostram que Vachellia caven correlaciona-se positivamente com condições de solo conferidas à área com pastoreio e negativamente com a biomassa aérea total do estrato herbáceo, o que comprova sua melhor adaptação ao pastoreio e intolerância aos maiores níveis de sombreamento do solo. É possível ainda inferir mediante análises exploratórias de ordenação (PCoA) que há uma total distinção entre as duas áreas de estudo, configurada pelas notáveis alterações ocorrentes ao longo de apenas cinco anos de exclusão nos componentes físicos do solo, estrato herbáceo e abundância de Prosopis affinis e Vachellia caven.

Main Points

The study was conducted in a fragment of Savana Estépica Parque (Parque Estadual do Espinilho, RS, Brazil), an area suitable for livestock activity due to its dense herbaceous stratum and isolated trees. The primary objective was to analyze floristic and edaphic alterations imposed by grazing.

Two distinct study areas were selected: one currently under grazing (A1) and one where grazing had been excluded for five years (A2). Both areas comprised a 2 ha sample unit, subdivided into 200 subunites of 100 m². Inventories of the arboreal and regenerating strata were carried out in 100 subunites, and other variables (soil physics, herbaceous biomass) were collected in 50 subunites. The analysis was split into two chapters: Chapter I focused on similarity, structural, and floristic changes; Chapter II evaluated physical soil properties, total aerial herbaceous biomass, and investigated correlations with the abundance of the two main regeneration species: *Prosopis affinis* and *Vachellia caven*.

Key findings revealed notable differences between the areas in terms of vegetation diameter structure and natural regeneration composition. The similarity between the areas, calculated using the Jaccard index, was moderate (75%). Significant differences between A1 and A2 were found in physical soil variables and total aerial herbaceous biomass, evidenced by Student’s T-tests. The Spearman correlation tests demonstrated a critical distinction between the two studied species: *Vachellia caven* was found to be the species better adapted to grazing, unlike *Prosopis affinis*. Specifically, *V. caven* correlated positively with the harsh soil conditions typical of the grazed area and negatively with the total aerial herbaceous biomass, suggesting intolerance to higher levels of soil shading.

Conclusions

The study concludes that the removal of grazing activity, even over a short period of five years, results in profound and measurable alterations in the Steppe Savanna Park ecosystem. There is a marked distinction between the grazed (A1) and protected (A2) areas, as confirmed by exploratory ordination analyses (PCoA), which captured changes in soil physical components, the herbaceous stratum, and the relative abundance of key species (*P. affinis* and *V. caven*).

The results highlight the superior adaptation of *Vachellia caven* to disturbances associated with livestock, including potentially compacted soil conditions and reduced herbaceous cover (less shading). Conversely, *Prosopis affinis* demonstrates sensitivity to grazing pressure. This differential adaptation directly influences the floristic composition and structural attributes of the natural regeneration layer. Ultimately, the research confirms that grazing is a dominant driver shaping the structure and composition of the natural vegetation and soil environment in this fragment of Savana Estépica Parque.

O Gênero Prosopis L. (Leguminosae Mimosoideae) NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL

Jose Newton Cardoso Marchiori, Solon J. Longhi, and Luiz Galvão (1983)

Abstract

No presente trabalho são descritas as duas especies do gênero Froe op i e nativas no Estado do Rio Grande do Sul: Fro e op i e aZg

Main Points

The study was conducted to clarify the identification, distribution, and botanical characteristics of native *Prosopis* species in Rio Grande do Sul (RS), Brazil, following expeditions in the Campanha region, particularly focusing on the Parque Espinilho area. The authors emphasize that existing scientific knowledge regarding the constituent species of this silvatic-campestre vegetation was insufficient, contributing to errors in official documents and hindering conservation efforts aimed at protecting the vegetation from extinction.

The main result was the confirmation and detailed description of two species: *Prosopis algarobilla* Gris. (Inhanduvã) and *Prosopis nigra* (Gris.) Hieron. (Algarrobo). Historically, only *P. algarobilla* was widely cited in the botanical literature of RS. The identification of *P. nigra* confirmed its status as native to the region, officially adding it to the flora of Rio Grande do Sul.

The authors provided differentiating morphological details. *P. algarobilla* typically exhibits a wide, flattened canopy, leaves with 1-4 cm long pinnas, and inflorescences larger than the leaves. It is described as having a broader distribution along the Ibicui River basin. In contrast, *P. nigra* tends toward an umbel-shaped canopy, has very short petioles (up to 2 cm), and inflorescences that are shorter than the leaves. Crucially for conservation, while *P. algarobilla* is typical of the Espinilho Park, *P. nigra* was found to be highly restricted in RS, observed only in the Espinilho Park near Barra do Quaraí, suggesting a localized presence and potential vulnerability. Both species provide durable wood, charcoal, and their fruits are noted as an important natural food source for livestock ("gado de pastoreio").

Conclusions

The analysis concluded that the native flora of Rio Grande do Sul includes two species of the genus *Prosopis*: *P. algarobilla* (Inhanduvã) and *P. nigra* (Algarrobo).

*P. algarobilla* was found to have a larger distribution area in RS than previously documented, notably along the Ibicui river basin. Morphologically, it is recognized by its wide and flattened canopy, leaves with 1, 2, or rarely 3 pairs of pinnas, and inflorescences that are longer than the leaves.

*P. nigra*, however, is confirmed to have a much more restricted distribution within the state, being found almost exclusively in the Parque Espinilho near the Barra do Quaraí. It is distinguished from *P. algarobilla* by its tendency towards an umbel-shaped canopy, longer petioles (up to 2 cm), leaves generally with 2–3 pairs of pinnas, and spike-like racemes that are shorter than the leaves.

This work was critical in formally establishing *P. nigra* as part of the native flora of RS, correcting historical botanical oversights, and providing necessary information for the conservation and accurate understanding of the threatened Espinilho Park vegetation.

ESTRUTURA FITOSSOCIOLÔGICA DE UMA ASSOCIAÇÃO NATURAL DE PARQUE INHANDUVÁ COM QUEBRACHO E CINA CINA, NO RIO GRANDE DO SUL·

J. L. Cardoso, J. N. C. Marchiori, N. G. Solon, S. J. Longhi, L. G. Galvão (1985)

Abstract

E estudada a estrutura fitossociolôgica de uma vegetação natural de Parque existente no extremo sudoeste do Estado do Rio Grande do Sul, em ãrea adjacente ao rio Quarai Chico e sob influin cia de sua mata ciliar. A vegetação caracteriza-se pela ocorrência expressiva de Aspidospe!'ma acuteata L. (cina-cina), o uab r a cho=b l an c o Schlecht. (quebracho) e de numerosas esp~ cies tipicas da mata ciliar, associadas com as tris espêcies de Inhanduvã. Por ser uma associação ún í c a no Brasi 1 e por constituir-se em um ecossistema muito frãgil, sugere-se a preservação do mesmo. UNITERMOS: FITOSSOCIOLOGIA, PARQUE ESPINILHO, PARQUE DE INHANOUVA.

Main Points

The study utilized phytosociological methods to analyze the structure of the Parque Inhanduvã, a natural park vegetation association located in the far southwest of Rio Grande do Sul, Brazil, adjacent to the Quaraí Chico River and under the influence of its riparian forest.

**Methods:** A 10m-wide belt transect (10 x 25 m sub-samples, grouped into 750 m² units) oriented North-South was used. For all trees and regeneration, measurements included circumference at breast height (CBH), total height, trunk height, and the radius of crown projection across four cardinal points. The calculated structural parameters included Abundance, Dominance, Frequency, and the Index of Importance Value (IVI) for each species across height and diameter classes. Natural regeneration included all individuals with a CBH less than 5 cm. The fisionomic description was supplemented by two diagrammatic profiles (vertical and horizontal projection) and photographs.

**Results:** The vegetation structure is primarily defined by five arboreal species: *Prosopis nigra* (inhanduvã), *Prosopis affinis* (algarrobo), *Aspidosperma quebracho-blanco* (quebracho), *Parkinsonia aculeata* (cina-cina), and *Acacia caven* (espinilho). The quebracho and cina-cina form an emergent stratum above the paucifoliate layer, which includes the *Prosopis* species and espinilho. The overall canopy is characterized by interpenetration but leaves significant open spaces. This structure facilitates the development of a dense herbaceous and grassy stratum, including species from genera like *Andropogon*, *Paspalum*, *Setaria*, and *Stipa*, as well as Compositae, Leguminosae, and Oxalidaceae. The association exhibits a xerophytic character (e.g., presence of *Opuntia bonaerensis* and thick, cracked bark). Furthermore, the area contains small circular 'islands' of larger trees and riparian species (*Scutia buxifolia*, *Guettarda uruguensis*), indicating influence from the adjacent ciliary forest.

Conclusions

The analysis successfully detailed the phytosociological structure of the Parque Inhanduvã association, confirming it as a unique and specific type of natural park formation within Brazil, related to the broader Mesopotamian Park formations. The dominant arboreal species, including *Acacia caven* (espinilho), are fundamental structural components defining the canopy stratification and contributing to the overall xerophytic morphology.

The primary finding leading to the conclusion is that this association is considered **"a rare association in Brazil"** and constitutes a **"very fragile ecosystem"**, occupying a highly restricted area in the extreme southwest of Rio Grande do Sul. Due to its scarcity and ecological vulnerability, the authors strongly recommend the preservation of this specific formation. This highlights the natural, structural importance of *Acacia caven* within this unique, threatened environment, supporting the argument that it is a key native component requiring conservation, not removal.

Supports Grazing and Land Use ImpactsPampas Ecosystem Degradation and ResilienceConservation and Restoration Strategies

Manual de Prácticas de Manejo del Monte Nativo

Rafael Alberto Sabattini; Norberto Muzzachiodi; Arturo Fabián Dorsch (2002)

Abstract

The provided text does not contain a single, formal abstract. The analysis below synthesizes the introductory sections (pp. 1-4) which serve as the problem statement and justification for the manual.

Main Points

### Problem Statement: Deforestation and Degradation

The text opens by characterizing the severe global and national deforestation crisis, noting that Argentina has lost two-thirds of its original forest patrimony. Between 1990 and 2000, 285,000 hectares were deforested annually, leading to projections of total extinction of native forests by 2025-2028. Specifically in Entre Ríos province, native woodlands (*montes nativos*) have decreased dramatically, from 2.5 million hectares to less than 500,000 hectares, or approximately 33% of the land surface according to some estimates.

In the Centro-Norte region of Entre Ríos, the remaining *montes* show significant deterioration. The authors explicitly identify the primary causes as *manejo tradicional de la ganadería* (traditional livestock management), which alters the forest's structure and composition, and unplanned agriculture. The specific impacts of traditional grazing include intensive pasturing, trampling (*pisoteo*), deficient drainage, and *enmalezamiento* (proliferation of weeds/bush), leading to deterioration across an estimated 800,000 hectares in the region.

### Proposed Solution: Agroforestry and Silvopastoral Systems

Given the limitations of the region’s soils for intensive traditional agriculture, the manual proposes the adoption of Silvopastoral systems (a form of Agroforestería) as a sustainable alternative. Agroforestería is presented as an interdisciplinary approach that integrates woody species with agricultural crops and/or livestock. The rationality of this technology is to optimize positive interactions between components and the physical environment, increasing total productivity, diversification, and profitability while protecting the soil resource.

The document stresses that replacing forests with monocultures (agriculture or pastures) truncates the regenerative cycle, causing soil nutrients to deplete rapidly and forcing further expansion into forest land. In contrast, integrating trees maintains ecosystem stability, prevents erosion and desertification, and supports the combined production of timber and forage, offering a path for the recovery and sustainable management of the native woodland resource. This work is based on prior research into silvopastoral management models conducted since 1996 in the region.

Conclusions

The core conclusion of the introductory sections is that the severe degradation of the native woodlands in Entre Ríos—characterized by massive historical deforestation, loss of productive capacity, and structural deterioration—is fundamentally a result of unsustainable, traditional agricultural and livestock management practices, particularly chronic overgrazing and unplanned deforestation.

This degradation results in negative ecological outcomes, including high risks of water erosion due to low soil stability and the consequent reduction in productive capacity. The authors stress that without proper planning and a shift away from traditional exploitation, the ecosystem will continue its decline.

Consequently, the manual’s central recommendation is to transition toward sustainable **silvopastoral ecosystems (Agroforestería)**. This approach is viewed as crucial because it offers an alternative productive vision that is non-contaminating and non-degrading. By consciously integrating trees, crops, and animals, the land use can maximize resource utilization, preserve biodiversity, maintain nutrient cycles, and protect soil stability, thereby ensuring the long-term persistence and productivity of the Espinal ecosystem, where species like Ñandubay (a key woody species) predominate.

Key Quotes

  • "La Argentina no escapa al decepcionante fenómeno de deforestación mundial, estimándose que ha perdido las dos terceras partes del patrimonio forestal original."
  • "En la provincia de Entre Ríos los montes nativos a principios de siglo ocupaban 2.500.000 millones de hectáreas y actualmente es menor a 500.000 ha (Spahn y Casermeiro, 1999)."
  • "En la región centro-norte los montes presentan diversos signos de deterioro provocados por el manejo tradicional de la ganadería que altera su estructura y composición, sumado a la agricultura sin una planificación previa."
  • "El manejo de montes para la producción silvopastoril ha generado creciente atención en los últimos años, por sus posibilidades en la producción maderera y forrajera, y su capacidad para la protección del recurso suelo (Sabattini et al., 2000b)."
  • "Uno de los problemas más importantes de la región es la falta de conocimiento sobre el manejo del recurso monte."
  • "El I.N.T.A. indica que en esta región existen alrededor de 800.000 ha que presentan distintos grados de deterioro, producido esencialmente por pastoreo intensivo, drenaje deficiente, pisoteo, y enmalezamiento, producto del pastoreo selectivo (PROSA, 1988)."

FACILITATION BY PIONEER TREES AND HERBIVORE EXCLUSION ALLOW REGENERATION AND SUCCESSION OF WOODY SPECIES IN A SEMIARID ECOSYSTEM

Nicolás Antonio Gómez Fernández (2020)

Abstract

In semiarid ecosystems, pioneer nurse plants facilitate regeneration of woody species, however, colonization in open areas and under nurse tree canopy could be limited by the presence of herbivores. The goal of this study was evaluated the effect of cattle and rabbit exclusion and the Acacia caven on natural regeneration of woody species, in a seven-year experiment in two localities (Pirque and Peñuelas) of central Chile. Six exclosures and control areas were established in degraded savannas of A. caven close to sclerophyllous forest fragments, where sexual and asexual (resprouts) regeneration was sampled in plots located under the canopy of A. caven and in open sites. After seven years, species richness and abundance of plants of sexual regeneration (size 0.5-2m) was significantly greater within exclosures than in control areas. Species richness and abundance of both type of regeneration was greater Under A. caven than in open sites in both localities. In Peñuelas, abundance of asexually regenerated seedlings was significantly greater within exclosures than in control areas, in both localities. In no variable or locality some significant effect of the interaction between A. caven and exclosure was detected. Our results suggest that when cattle and rabbits are present, the use of exclosures may allow colonization of open sites and successional advance under canopy of Acacia caven. Instead, asexual regeneration does not seem to be importantly affected by herbivores, and hence it may contribute to recover this forest when exclusion of large surfaces is not possible.

Main Points

The study utilized a seven-year experimental design (2010–2017) across two central Chilean localities, Pirque (pre-Andean) and Peñuelas (coastal), to test the independent and combined effects of herbivore exclusion (cattle and rabbits) and facilitation by the pioneer tree *Acacia caven* on the natural regeneration of woody species.

Six 30 x 40 m exclosures and corresponding unfenced control areas were established in degraded *A. caven* savannas situated near native sclerophyllous forest fragments. Regeneration was sampled in plots located either under the canopy of *A. caven* (nurse effect) or in open sites, allowing for the analysis of four treatment combinations. The data collected between 2012 and 2017 included both sexual regeneration (from seed germination) and asexual regeneration (resprouts).

Key results demonstrated strong positive effects from both exclusion and facilitation. After seven years, species richness and abundance of sexually regenerated plants (specifically those 0.5–2m in height) were significantly greater inside the exclosures than in control areas. Supporting the nurse plant hypothesis, species richness and abundance of both sexual and asexual regeneration types were consistently greater under the canopy of *A. caven* compared to open sites in both study locations. Although sexual regeneration benefited markedly from exclusion, in Peñuelas, asexual regeneration abundance was also significantly greater within exclosures. Crucially, the researchers did not detect a significant interaction effect between the presence of *A. caven* and herbivore exclusion, suggesting these two positive restoration drivers acted largely independently.

Conclusions

The study concludes that the lack of successional advancement and the slow recovery rate observed in degraded *A. caven* savannas in central Chile are driven by two main factors: harsh environmental conditions in open areas and high herbivory pressure from introduced mammals like cattle and rabbits.

The findings strongly confirm the crucial role of *A. caven* as a nurse plant, significantly facilitating the regeneration and recruitment of native woody species beneath its canopy by ameliorating environmental stress. This facilitation is essential for the colonization of mid and late-successional species. The research highlights that successful forest restoration requires overcoming the limitation imposed by herbivory, as evidenced by the significantly improved regeneration richness and abundance within exclosures.

Consequently, the authors recommend that when cattle and rabbits are present, the implementation of exclosures is necessary to allow for the colonization of open sites and to promote successional advance under the existing *A. caven* canopy. They also suggest that while exclusion primarily benefits sexual regeneration, asexual regeneration (resprouting) is less impacted by herbivores and can therefore serve as an important pathway for forest recovery in scenarios where fencing large areas is not feasible.

Key Quotes

  • "One of the main anthropic drivers limiting recovering of native forest has been the herbivory of introduced mammals, like cattle horses and the European rabbit (Nomiya et al., 2003; Fensham et al., 2011)."
  • "After seven years, species richness and abundance of plants of sexual regeneration (size 0.5-2m) was significantly greater within exclosures than in control areas."
  • "Species richness and abundance of both type of regeneration was greater Under A. caven than in open sites in both localities."
  • "Most degraded natural areas became open grasslands, which in many cases, have been colonized by the native tree Acacia caven (Mol.) Mol., forming savannas at early successional stages."
  • "However, most of these savannas show no evidence of successional advancement or recovery of the original forest (Ovalle et al., 2006; Van de Wouw et al., 2011)."
  • "Presence of these woody pioneer plants may reduce water stress and increase soil nutrient availability, which may become crucial for regeneration of mid and late-successional species (Calle & Holl, 2019; Cuevas et al., 2013; Devaney et al., 2014)."
  • "Despite A. caven savannas are characteristics of degraded ecosystems (Ovalle et al., 1996), they can provide ecological conditions to trigger restoration processes since A. caven trees may act as nurse plants facilitating the recruitment of herbaceous and woody species under their canopy..."
  • "The goal of this study was to assess the effect of cattle and rabbit exclusion and the role of A. caven in the natural regeneration of woody native species of the Sclerophyllous forest of central Chile..."
  • "Our results suggest that when cattle and rabbits are present, the use of exclosures may allow colonization of open sites and successional advance under canopy of Acacia caven."

The legacy of the extinct Neotropical megafauna on plants and biomes

Vinicius L. Dantas & Juli G. Pausas (2022)

Abstract

Large mammal herbivores are important drivers of plant evolution and vegetation patterns, but the extent to which plant trait and ecosystem geography currently reﬂect the historical distribution of extinct megafauna is unknown. We address this question for South and Central America (Neotropical biogeographic realm) by compiling data on plant defence traits, cli-mate, soil, and ﬁre, as well as on the historical distribution of extinct megafauna and extant mammal herbivores. We show that historical mammal herbivory, especially by extinct megafauna, and soil fertility explain substantial variability in wood density, leaf size, spines and latex. We also identiﬁed three distinct regions (‘‘antiherbiomes’’), differing in plant defences, environmental conditions, and megafauna history. These patterns largely matched those observed in African ecosystems, where abundant megafauna still roams, and suggest that some ecoregions experienced savanna-to-forest shifts following megafauna extinctions. Here, we show that extinct megafauna left a signiﬁcant imprint on current ecosystem biogeography.

Main Points

The study analyzed the influence of extinct Neotropical megafauna (130,000 to 1500 CE) on current plant functional traits and biome geography across South and Central America. The authors compiled ecoregion-level data for five antiherbivory defense traits in woody species: wood density, leaf size, spinescence (leaf and stem), and latex production. These traits were correlated with megafauna metrics (richness, body mass, and diet type—grazer, browser, mixed feeder), extant herbivore data, and environmental variables (climate, soil, fire).

Results indicated that megafauna history, particularly richness and the ratio of grazers to browsers, explained substantial variability in antiherbivory traits. Specifically, wood density and leaf spines increased, while leaf size decreased, with higher megafauna richness. The occurrence of mega-grazers relative to browsers was a key driver for investment in dense wood and spines. Stem spines were best explained by mid-size megafauna body mass and high soil pH (alkaline soils).

The researchers used PCA to define three "antiherbiomes" based on convergent defense strategies: (1) Small Leaves Thorny (SLT), characterized by high defenses (thorns, small leaves, wood density), arid/cold conditions, nutrient-rich soils, and a high density of extinct large grazers; (2) Broad Chemically-defended Leaves (BCL), featuring large, chemically defended leaves, moist climates, and few, large mega-browsers; and (3) Intermediate Leaves Woody (ILW), defined by very high wood density, intermediate traits, moist/hot climates, and nutrient-poor soils. The study identified 27 forest-dominated ecoregions (covering 6.4 million Km²) that were likely grassy ecosystems during the Pleistocene, based on their high richness of megafauna grazers and classification into the SLT or ILW antiherbiomes. This confirms massive savanna-to-forest biome shifts post-extinction.

Conclusions

The authors conclude that the long-term impact of extinct Neotropical megafauna is profoundly reflected in current patterns of plant defense trait geography and ecosystem distribution. This supports the hypothesis that large mammal herbivores are essential drivers of ecosystem structure, and their historical absence resulted in lasting ecological shifts, often seen as *anachronical* defense traits persisting in modern flora.

The research established that South-Central America and Africa shared similar ecological pressures mediated by megafauna and soil fertility, leading to the formation of recognizable antiherbiomes across both continents. Crucially, the identification of the high-defense SLT and ILW antiherbiomes in areas now dominated by forest provides strong evidence for extensive savanna-to-forest biome shifts following the late Pleistocene megafauna extinction. These findings suggest that the functional structure of many Neotropical ecosystems today is primarily a relic of past intense herbivory pressure, providing critical insights for understanding recent dynamics and shifts in Neotropical biomes.

Key Quotes

  • "We show that historical mammal herbivory, especially by extinct megafauna, and soil fertility explain substantial variability in wood density, leaf size, spines and latex."
  • "Here, we show that extinct megafauna left a signiﬁcant imprint on current ecosystem biogeography."
  • "Consequently, their extinction likely resulted in the replacement of many herbivory-maintained savannas by forests and woodlands, or by ﬁre-maintained savannas, across the world7,8."
  • "Woody plant species living in herbivory-maintained ecosystems are characterised by morphological and physiological adaptations that reduce damage caused by large herbivores (i.e., antiherbivory defence traits)7."
  • "While defence traits that are dis-advantageous under present conditions were likely lost in many places after megafauna extinction... other traits may have persisted as anachronical features9,10."
  • "Given the long history of megafauna presence and the short history of its absence, we hypothesised that the distribution of extinct megafauna left an imprint on current patterns of plant functional trait geography."
  • "We predicted that the distribution of defence traits in the Neotropics would broadly coincide with the historical distribution of large mammal herbivores in this region."
  • "Wood density and leaf spines increased, whereas leaf size decreased, with megafauna richness..."
  • "The occurrence of more extinct megafauna grazers relative to browsers was an important driver of investments in defence such as wood density and spines..."
  • "The Small Leaves Thorny (SLT) antiherbiome was characterized by thorny and small-leaved species, as well as arid, cold and nutrient-rich ecosystems, containing numerous extinct large grazers..."

Misaligned Narrative of the Ecological Role of Vachellia caven in Eastern South American Savannas

()

Abstract

Vachellia caven is a thorny leguminous shrub to treelet, widely distributed throughout the Neotropics and spanning across the Southern Cone from Bolivia, Paraguay and Brazil to Tierra del Fuego in Argentina and Chile. Most of the contemporary research focuses on the western range of the species distribution, in Chile, though this review emphasizes the species' long-term and widespread ecological importance in the eastern range, particularly within the Pampas of Southern South America. The Pampas is one of the most threatened open vegetation ecosystems, rapidly losing native habitats due to intense conversion for agriculture and livestock production. Driven by historical land use practices and the vast areas designated for livestock, xeric and spiny vegetation has long been suppressed and actively removed, as part of pasture management strategies. This review challenges the prevailing narrative that portrays V. caven as a controversial or ambiguous species, frequently labeled as "invasive woody encroacher". This designation, often documented in regions severely affected by conversion and overgrazing, reflects a socio-economic bias that emphasizes its purported negative impact on forage production while overlooking its ecological significance. The observed woody encroachment is fundamentally perceived as a symptom of anthropogenic degradation, including the historical removal of woody vegetation and chronic overgrazing. In contrast to this exploitative view, this xeric species acts as a crucial pioneer and "nurse" plant, essential for ecological succession and for sustaining a unique assemblage of native plants and animals. It facilitates the recruitment of other woody and herbaceous species by improving microhabitat conditions, including nitrogen enrichment and enhanced soil properties. By reframing V. caven’s encroachment as an indicator of ecosystem degradation rather than species invasiveness, we challenge the prevalent narrative that supports active removal of V. caven while underestimating its natural distributional range. Recognizing this species as fundamental to Pampas’ resilience and recovery is therefore essential for effective conservation and the development of sustainable restoration strategies.

Main Points

This review primarily functions by reframing the ecological interpretation of *Vachellia caven* within the Pampas ecosystem. Unlike standard primary research, this text summarizes findings from a review process, focusing on synthesizing existing literature to challenge prevailing management paradigms.

### Findings and Reinterpretations

1. **Geographical Shift:** The review intentionally shifts focus from the heavily studied western range of *V. caven* (Chile) to its long-term ecological importance in the eastern range, specifically the Pampas, an ecosystem critically threatened by conversion to agriculture and intensive livestock production.
2. **Socio-economic Bias Critique:** The research identifies that the widespread classification of *V. caven* as an "invasive woody encroacher" stems from historical land use practices and a socio-economic bias rooted in pasture management strategies. This bias prioritizes forage production, leading to the historical suppression and active removal of xeric and spiny vegetation.
3. **Reframing Encroachment:** The central finding is that observed woody encroachment should not be interpreted as species invasiveness, but rather as a *symptom* of anthropogenic degradation. This degradation includes chronic overgrazing and the historical suppression and removal of native woody vegetation.
4. **Positive Ecological Role:** In direct contrast to the negative portrayal, the review highlights the vital ecological function of the species. *V. caven* acts as a "crucial pioneer and 'nurse' plant," essential for ecological succession. It facilitates the recruitment of native plants and animals by improving microhabitat conditions, notably through nitrogen enrichment and general enhancement of soil properties.

Conclusions

The core conclusion of the review is that the prevalent narrative supporting the active removal of *Vachellia caven* is fundamentally flawed and based on an exploitative, socio-economic perspective that ignores its natural role and ecological significance.

First, the review concludes that by mislabeling the species as invasive, land managers and conservationists underestimate its natural distributional range and its inherent value to the ecosystem. The phenomenon of encroachment is merely an indicator signaling severe environmental stress and degradation, specifically chronic overgrazing and historical woody removal.

Secondly, the authors conclude that recognition of *V. caven* as a keystone species—fundamental to the resilience and recovery of the Pampas—is absolutely essential. Effective conservation and the development of sustainable restoration strategies must move beyond the bias against woody vegetation and incorporate the species' nurse effects. This recognition is necessary to successfully manage and restore one of the most threatened open vegetation ecosystems in South America.

Key Quotes

  • "This review challenges the prevailing narrative that portrays V. caven as a controversial or ambiguous species, frequently labeled as "invasive woody encroacher"."
  • "The Pampas is one of the most threatened open vegetation ecosystems, rapidly losing native habitats due to intense conversion for agriculture and livestock production."
  • "Driven by historical land use practices and the vast areas designated for livestock, xeric and spiny vegetation has long been suppressed and actively removed, as part of pasture management strategies."
  • "This designation, often documented in regions severely affected by conversion and overgrazing, reflects a socio-economic bias that emphasizes its purported negative impact on forage production while overlooking its ecological significance."
  • "The observed woody encroachment is fundamentally perceived as a symptom of anthropogenic degradation, including the historical removal of woody vegetation and chronic overgrazing."

  • "Recognizing this species as fundamental to Pampas’ resilience and recovery is therefore essential for effective conservation and the development of sustainable restoration strategies."

APROVECHAMIENTO SOSTENIBLE DE ÁREAS DE ESPINILLO: aprendiendo de experiencias en el litoral del Uruguay

Ing. Agr. Jorge Azziz1, Ing. Agr. Agustín Boffano2, Ing. Agr. Mateo Ceriani1, Ing. Agr. Joaquín Laborde3, Ing. Agr. Verónica Pastorini4, Ing. Agr. Joaquín Lapetina5 (2023)

Abstract

Este artículo sistematiza la colaboración entre productores e instituciones que se realizó durante el primer semestre de 2023, en torno al aprovechamiento sostenible de áreas de espinillo en el litoral del país. Los resultados de este trabajo pretenden ser un insumo para nuevas iniciativas que profundicen el abordaje en términos ecológicos, productivos y de gestión de estas áreas.

Main Points

The study systematizes inter-institutional collaboration and producer experiences (January to July 2023) focused on the sustainable management of *espinillo* (*Vachellia caven*) areas in the Uruguayan littoral. The motivation stems from the recognition that *espinillo* is a native forest component and a primary colonizer that often signals the native forest's attempt to reclaim space after disturbance. However, dense colonization (affecting approximately 30,000 hectares of INC land) presents a challenge, leading to contrasting management behaviors—some producers seek total elimination, while others seek integration.

In response to this conflict, institutional partners (INC, INIA, MGAP divisions, Udelar, etc.) collaborated to promote integrated systems where *espinillo* acts in synergy with pastures and livestock. The main methodological axis was a field day in May 2023, where 130 participants visited three successful management cases.

Case A (Pablo Gauthier, dairy) implemented management by maintaining tree rows (9 to 16 meters apart) to promote apical dominance, controlling inter-row regrowth with three annual passes of a rotative cutter, combined with strategic pasture resting. Case B (José Heit, mixed system) practiced controlled thinning (raleos) and pruning within typical park forest areas (espinillo and algarrobo) to balance tree cover, herbaceous growth, and controlled firewood extraction. Case C (Grupo Los Costeros, ranching) focused on restoring agricultural degraded land by combining varied tree densities with native pasture promotion, including experimental sowing of *Paspalum notatum - INIA Sepé* (a pioneer graminea), using adequate pasture rest periods to encourage competition against regrowth. The collaboration concluded by producing a specific publication and a guidance booklet (cartilla).

Conclusions

The management of *espinillo* areas is a complex issue of concern to producers, technicians, and institutions, requiring an important integration of disciplines (ecology, agronomy, economy, sociology).

The results confirm that promising outcomes can be achieved by reconciling production interests with conservation goals, although such experiences are still infrequent. Crucially, the authors conclude that greater knowledge about the ecology of *espinillo*—as a component of the park forest—is essential for establishing good management and conservation practices, especially in low-aptitude agricultural soils.

Key areas needing further development include systematized data on management costs, better indicators and sustainability criteria for forest management, and the valuation of ecosystem services provided by these systems (e.g., nitrogen fixation, carbon capture, soil restoration, biodiversity contribution). The study highlights the significant opportunity to redesign and manage marginal agricultural areas with *espinillo* using a whole-farm system approach focused on resource conservation, stressing that basing these systems on native trees and pastures is key to building sustainability and resilience against climate change.

  • "El espinillo (Vachellia caven) es una especie arbórea componente del ecosistema del bosque nativo de la región."
  • "Es la primera colonizadora luego de un disturbio del suelo y/o del bosque, es decir que, en ocasiones, su presencia significa una respuesta del bosque nativo por recuperar espacios que posiblemente ocupó antiguamente."
  • "Actualmente existen comportamientos contrastantes: productores que buscan eliminar por completo dichas zonas, buscando el cambio de uso de suelo, y quienes buscan adaptar alguna técnica de manejo, disminuyendo la densidad arbórea."
  • "El espinillo tiene la capacidad de aportar una variedad de servicios ecosistémicos, que podrían ser capitalizados con un manejo adecuado: confort térmico para el ganado..., fijación de nitrógeno, captación de agua, captura y conservación de carbono, provisión de leña, reservorio de biodiversidad, entre otros."

  • "“Hay que amigarse con el espinillo y destinar los esfuerzos a formar el árbol (raleo y conducción) y así evitar lo más posible el rebrote por yemas desde las raíces. Por otra parte, el empotreramiento y manejo del pastoreo es el gran paso para contar con la pastura como herramienta que compita con el rebrote del espinillo”"
  • "“Con descansos adecuados de la pastura, es posible favorecer al tapiz y que compita con el espinillo para lograr un equilibrio. Apuntamos a una mejor cobertura del suelo, un mayor volumen de pasto y un mejor resultado ganadero”"
